Ruling on Mut'ah for a Divorced Woman Without Mahr
Establishes the obligation and amount of mut'ah for woman divorced before consummation without specified dower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of mut'ah for a divorced woman without mahr, identify its components (three garments), and explain the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib for a woman divorced before consummation without a mahr; it consists of three garments suited to her status.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah – a compensatory gift for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was agreed. The Quran explicitly commands provision for such women, and the Prophet's practice confirms the obligation and the quantity. We will unpack the text, the evidence, and the legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the conditions: divorce occurs before consummation or valid seclusion, and no mahr (dower) was specified in the marriage contract.
Khalwah (seclusion) is equivalent to consummation in establishing full mahr, but here we focus on cases without mahr specification.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling: mut'ah is wajib (obligatory) upon the husband in this scenario. The hukm level is wajib, not fard, due to the nature of the evidence (imperative in Quran, but zanni in dalala according to some interpretations).
The obligation is derived from the imperative verb 'matti'uhunna' in Quran 2:236.
3
Determine the quantity and quality
The minimum mut'ah is three garments: a chemise (dir'), a head scarf (khimar), and a wrapper (milhafah). The garments must be appropriate to the woman's social status (e.g., if she is wealthy, high-quality cloth; if poor, simple cloth).
Some scholars allow equivalent value if garments are not suitable.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
Surah al-Baqarah 2:236 commands: '...and provide for them, the wealthy according to his means and the poor according to his means, a provision in an acceptable manner, a duty upon the doers of good.' The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The verse is qat'i in thubut (transmission) but zanni in dalala (meaning), hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
5
Examine the Prophetic practice
The hadith of 'Amrah bint al-Jun reports that the Prophet divorced her before consummation and gave her three Razigi garments as mut'ah. This confirms the obligation and the specific quantity.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah; the chain is sound (hasan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخلوة فلها المتعة وهى ثلثة اثواب من كسوة مثلها وهي درع وخمار وملحفة ۱۷۸۴ (۵۹) اگر عورت کے لئے مہر متعین نہ کیا ہو اور اس کو صحبت یا خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دے دی ہو تو ایسی عورت کو متعہ ملے گا ۔ اور متعہ میں تین کپڑے ہوتے ہیں۔ عورت کا کرتا اور اوڑھنی اور چادر ۔ اس میں جس معیار کی عورت ہوگی اسی معیار کا کپڑادیا جائے گا۔ آیت میں ہے کہ ایسی عورت کو متعہ دیا جائے گا۔ لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوا لهن فريضة ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره متاعا بالمعروف حقا على المحسنين (آیت ۲۳۶ سورة البقرة ٢) اس آیت کی تفسیر عبداللہ بن عباس سے یوں ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس في هذه الآية قال هو الرجل يتزوج المرأة ولم يسم لها صداقا ثم طلقها من قبل ان ينكحها فامر الله تعالى ان يمتعها على قدر يسره وعسره فان كان موسرا متعها بخادم او نحو ذلك وان كان معسرا فبثلاثة اثواب او نحو ذلك (الف) (سنن ؟ للبیہقی ، باب التفويض، کتاب الصداق ج سابع ص ۳۹۸، نمبر ۱۴۴۰۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس عورت کے لئے مہر متعین نہ ہو اور صحبت سے پہلے طلاق ہو جائے اس کو متعہ دینا واجب ہے۔ اور اس اثر سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ متعہ تین کپڑے ہیں۔ حضور نے صحبت سے پہلے عمرہ بنت جون کو طلاق دی تو تین کپڑے متعہ دیا۔ عن عائشة ان عمرة بنت الجون تعوذت من رسول الله الله . حين ادخلت عليه فقال لقد عذت بمعاذ فطلقها وامر اسامة او انسا فمتعها بثلاثة اثواب رازقية (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب متعة الطلاق ص ۲۹۲ نمبر ۲۰۳۷)
And if there is seclusion, then she has the mut'ah, and it is three garments of her like clothing: a chemise, a head scarf, and a wrapper. [1784] (59) If a woman's mahr was not specified and he divorced her before intercourse or seclusion, then such a woman will receive mut'ah. And mut'ah consists of three garments: the woman's chemise, head scarf, and wrapper. The garment will be given according to the standard of the woman. The verse says that such a woman should be given mut'ah: 'There is no blame upon you if you divorce women before you have touched them or specified for them an obligation. And provide for them, the wealthy according to his means and the poor according to his means, a provision in an acceptable manner, a duty upon the doers of good.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236). The interpretation of this verse from Abdullah ibn Abbas is: He said: It is about a man who marries a woman and does not name a dower for her, then divorces her before consummating the marriage. So Allah commanded him to provide her mut'ah according to his ease or hardship. If he is wealthy, he provides her with a servant or the like; if he is poor, then three garments or the like. (Reported by al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Tafwid, Kitab al-Sadaq, vol. 7, p. 398, no. 14405). From this it is understood that giving mut'ah is wajib for a woman who has no specified mahr and is divorced before intercourse. And from this athar it is also understood that mut'ah is three garments. The Prophet divorced 'Amrah bint al-Jun before consummation and gave her three garments as mut'ah. From 'Aisha: 'Amrah bint al-Jun sought refuge from Allah's Messenger when she was brought in to him, so he said: 'You have sought refuge from the One who grants refuge.' So he divorced her and ordered Usamah or Anas to give her three garments of Razigi cloth as mut'ah. (Ibn Majah, Bab Mut'at al-Talaq, p. 292, no. 2037).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the obligation of mut'ah for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. The author states that if there has been seclusion (khalwah) as well, she still gets mut'ah. The amount is three garments: a dress (dir'), a headscarf (khimar), and a wrapper (milhafah). The garments must be appropriate to the woman's social status. The Quranic proof is verse 2:236, which commands provision for such women. The author then cites the tafsir of Ibn Abbas, who explains that the verse applies to a man who marries a woman without naming a dower and then divorces her before consummation. The mut'ah is wajib according to this ruling. The Prophet's practice is also cited: when 'Amrah bint al-Jun sought refuge from him, he divorced her and gave her three garments as mut'ah. This confirms the obligation and the quantity.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman when no mahr was specified and before consummation or seclusion.
الخلوة (al-khalwah): Valid seclusion between husband and wife that implies full mahr in the absence of intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When she is divorced before consummation with no mahr specified
B) When she is divorced after consummation with mahr specified
C) When she is divorced after consummation without mahr
D) When she is divorced before consummation with mahr specified

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is a wajib consolatory gift of three garments for a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr, based on Quran and Sunnah.

Marriage with Wine or Pig as Mahr: Validity and Substitute Dower
Ruling on marriage with wine or pig as mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with an invalid mahr (wine or pig) and explain how mahr al-mithl is substituted.

Core Idea
The marriage contract is valid even if the mahr is forbidden; an invalid mahr is void and replaced by mahr al-mithl.

What happens if a Muslim man marries a woman on the understanding that her dower will be wine or a pig? The specified items are clearly impermissible in Islam. Does this invalidate the entire marriage? The Hanafi school provides a clear answer: the marriage itself remains valid because the contract is sound, but the specified mahr is void, and the woman is entitled to the proper dower of her peers (mahr al-mithl). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the proof from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a marriage contract where the mahr is specified as wine or pig. The ruling is that the marriage is valid (sahih).
This is the core ruling: the validity of the contract is independent of the validity of the mahr specification.
2
Examine why the specified mahr is invalid
Wine and pig are not considered property (mal) for a Muslim because they are impure and cannot be owned or sold. Therefore, specifying them as mahr has no legal effect.
The Hanafi definition of mal excludes forbidden substances; thus the mahr is fasid (defective).
3
Apply the consequence of an unspecified mahr
When the mahr is invalid, it is as if no mahr was specified. In that case, the general rule (from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud) applies: the woman gets mahr al-mithl, the dower of women of similar status.
This is based on the principle from issue no. 57 referenced in the source: when no mahr is fixed, mahr al-mithl is due.
4
Analyze the proof: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
The author cites the hadith where Ibn Mas'ud ruled that a woman whose husband died before specifying a dower receives mahr al-mithl, with no reduction or excess. This hadith is the dalil for the ruling on unspecified mahr.
The hadith is reported by Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud; it provides the wajh al-dalalah (legal link) that absence of a valid mahr triggers mahr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجها المسلم على خمر او خنزير فالنكاح جائز ولها مهر مثلها ۱۷۸۳ (۵۹) اگر عورت سے مسلمان نے شراب یا سور پر شادی کی تو نکاح جائز ہے اور عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہے۔ شراب اور سور مسلمان کے لئے مال نہیں ہیں اس لئے اس پر شادی کرنا گویا کہ مہر نہیں متعین کرتا ہے۔ اور جب مہر متعین نہیں کیا تو مسئلہ نمبر ۵۷ کی رو سے اس پر مہر مثل لازم ہوگا۔ اور حدیث گزر چکی ہے عن ابن مسعود انه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقا ولم يدخل بها حتى مات فقال ابن مسعود لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط الخ (ج) ( ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء في الرجل يتزوج المرأة فیموت عنها قبل اى يفرض لها ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۱۴۵ رابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۲۱۱۴)
And if a Muslim man marries her on (the basis of) wine or a pig, then the marriage is valid and she has her mahr al-mithl (like the mahr of her peers). [1783] (59) If a Muslim married a woman on (the basis of) wine or a pig, then the marriage is valid and the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl. Wine and pig are not property (mal) for a Muslim, therefore marrying on them is like not specifying a mahr. And when no mahr was specified, then according to issue no. 57, mahr al-mithl becomes incumbent. And the hadith has passed: from Ibn Mas'ud that he was asked about a man who married a woman and did not specify a dower for her, and he died before entering upon her. Ibn Mas'ud said: She has the mahr of the women of her family, no reduction and no excess. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-rajul yatazawwaju al-mar'ah, p. 217, no. 1145; Abu Dawud, no. 2114).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the validity of a marriage contract where the mahr is specified as wine or pig. According to Hanafi fiqh, such a marriage is valid because the contract itself is not voided by an invalid mahr specification. However, since wine and pig are not considered property (mal) for a Muslim—they are impure and impermissible to own—the specified mahr is void. Therefore, it is as if no mahr was specified. In that case, the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper dower equivalent to that of her peers). The author cites the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud to support the principle that when no mahr is specified, mahr al-mithl is due. This ruling shows that the validity of nikah does not depend on the validity of the mahr; rather, the mahr is an independent obligation that is rectified if initially invalid.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to that given to women of similar status (family, beauty, etc.) in the community.
مال (mal): Property that has value (mutamawwal) and is permissible to use in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a Muslim marries with wine as the mahr?
A) The marriage is batil and invalid
B) The marriage is valid but the wife gets mahr al-mithl
C) The marriage is valid and the wife gets the wine
D) The marriage is fasid and must be renewed

Key Takeaway
When a marriage contract specifies an invalid mahr (like wine or pig), the marriage remains valid and the woman receives mahr al-mithl.

Later Agreement on Mahr After Marriage
Ruling on later agreement/increase of mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the binding nature of a mahr agreed upon after marriage and distinguish the consequences based on whether consummation or death occurs, or divorce before consummation.

Core Idea
A mahr agreed after marriage binds only after consummation or death; before that, only mut'ah is due on divorce.

What happens if a couple marries without specifying a mahr? Can they later agree on an amount, and is that agreement binding? This lesson presents a foundational Hanafi ruling that clarifies these questions. It also covers cases where the husband increases the mahr after the contract. Understanding these rules is essential for determining the wife's rights in scenarios where the mahr is not fixed at the time of the marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three distinct situations: (1) no mahr named at marriage, then spouses later agree on an amount; (2) divorce before consummation/seclusion without a specified mahr; (3) husband increases the mahr after the contract.
These are separate rulings that may apply in different contexts.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For (1) the agreed mahr is for the wife if the husband consummates or dies; for (2) the wife gets mut'ah (a gift of consolation), not half of the agreed mahr; for (3) the increase is binding upon consummation or death.
The binding condition is consistent across scenarios (1) and (3).
3
Understand the triggering condition
The agreement or increase becomes binding only after consummation (al-dukhul) or the husband's death. Before those events, the wife's right is limited: if divorce occurs, she receives mut'ah instead of the agreed amount.
This distinguishes later agreement from a mahr specified at the time of contract, where half is due upon pre-consummation divorce.
4
Distinguish from specified mahr at contract
When mahr is fixed at the time of contract, divorce before consummation entitles the wife to half of that mahr. In contrast, for later agreement without consummation/death, she receives only mut'ah.
The difference arises because the later agreement is conditional on subsequent events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهرا ثم تراضيا على تسمية مهر فهو لها ان دخل بها او مات عنها [ ١٨۶ ] (٦١ وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها والخلوة فلها المتعة [۱۷۸۷ (۶۲) وان زاد في المهر بعد العقد لزمته الزيادة ان دخل بها او مات
And if he marries her and does not name a mahr for her, then they mutually agree on naming a mahr, then it is for her if he enters upon her or dies from her. [1785] (60) And if he divorces her before entering upon her and before seclusion, then she has mut'ah. [1787] (62) And if he increases the mahr after the contract, the increase is binding upon him if he enters upon her or dies.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement covering three scenarios: (1) When no mahr was specified at the time of marriage, but later the spouses mutually agree on a specific amount. In this case, that agreed amount becomes the mahr due, and it is binding if the husband consummates the marriage or dies. This is because the agreement replaces the lack of specification. (2) If the husband divorces before consummation or seclusion, she gets mut'ah instead of half of the agreed mahr, because the original mahr was not specified. (3) If after the contract, the husband increases the mahr, that increase becomes binding upon consummation or death. The text here is brief and serves as a memorization anchor for these basic rules.

Key Terms
تراضيا (taradaya): Mutual consent and agreement between the spouses on the mahr amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Spouses agree on a mahr after marriage. Which event(s) make the agreed mahr binding?
A) Marriage contract
B) Consummation or death of husband
C) Birth of a child
D) Agreement alone

Key Takeaway
A mahr agreed upon after marriage becomes binding and due in full only upon consummation or the husband's death; otherwise, only mut'ah is due on divorce.

Mut'ah After Later Mahr Agreement
Ruling on mut'ah after later mahr agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a later mahr agreement does not trigger half-mahr upon pre-consummation divorce, and justify it with Quran 2:236.

Core Idea
Later mahr agreement is not retroactive; pre-consummation divorce triggers mut'ah, not half.

In Hanafi nikah, if no mahr is specified at contract, the marriage is still valid. The couple may later agree on a mahr, but this agreement only takes effect after consummation or death. If divorce occurs before consummation, the wife receives mut'ah (a gift), not half the later-agreed amount. This lesson unpacks the logic and proof from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage considers: marriage without mahr specification, then mutual agreement on a mahr, followed by pre-consummation divorce. Recognize that this is a specific scenario within the broader rules of mahr.
The marriage contract itself is valid even without mahr.
2
State the ruling
The ruling: the wife is entitled to mut'ah, not half the later-agreed mahr. Contrast with the default rule: if mahr was specified at contract and divorce before consummation, she gets half.
Mut'ah is a gift, determined by the husband's capacity.
3
Identify the legal reasoning
Why no half? Because the later agreement is not part of the original contract; it only becomes binding upon consummation or death. Since divorce occurs before that, the agreement has no effect.
This is a Hanafi specific principle: later specification does not retroactively fix the original missing mahr.
4
Connect to the Quranic proof
The verse (2:236) explicitly commands mut'ah for women divorced before being touched and before specification of a 'fareedah' (obligation). Since no mahr was specified at contract, this verse directly applies.
The later agreement does not constitute a 'fareedah' at the time of the verse's application.
5
Distinguish from related scenarios
Note that if consummation or death occurs after the later agreement, the full agreed mahr is wajib. Also, if no mahr is ever agreed, the wife gets mahr al-mithl. Understand the boundaries.
This case sits between no mahr and full mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهرا ثم تراضيا على تسمية مهر فهو لها ان دخل بها او مات عنها [ ١٨۶ ] (٦١ وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها والخلوة فلها المتعة [۱۷۸۷ (۶۲) اگر عورت سے شادی کی اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں کیا بعد میں دونوں راضی ہو گئے تو صحبت کرنے کے بعد یا شوہر کے انتقال کے بعد وہی مہر لازم ہو گا جس پر دونوں راضی ہو گئے ہیں۔ مہر مثل اس وقت واجب ہوتا ہے جب کچھ بھی طے نہ ہو اور یہاں بعد میں ایک مقدار طے کر لی اور عورت اس پر راضی ہو گئی اس لئے مہر مثل لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ جو طے ہوا ہے وہی لازم ہوگا۔ [۱۷۸۶ (۶۱) اگر اس کو طلاق دی صحبت سے پہلے اور خلوت سے پہلے تو اس کے لئے متعہ ہے۔ عورت کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں تھا۔ بعد میں کسی مقدار پر راضی ہو گئے ایسی صورت میں صحبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دے دی تو اس مقدار کا آدھا نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس کے لئے متعہ ہوگا۔ چونکہ نکاح کے وقت مہر متعین نہیں کیا بعد میں مقدار متعین کی ہے اس لئے اس متعینہ مقدار کا آدھا نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مہر متعین نہیں ہے اس لئے بغیر خلوت کے طلاق دی ہے تو اس کے لئے صرف متعہ ہو گا (۲) آیت گزر چکی ہے لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوا لهن فريضة ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره (الف) (آیت ۲۳۶ سورة البقرة ٢)
And if he marries her and does not name a mahr for her, then they mutually agree on naming a mahr, then it is for her if he enters upon her or dies from her. [1785] (60) And if he divorces her before entering upon her and before seclusion, then she has mut'ah. [1787] (62) If a man married a woman and did not specify a mahr for her, later both agreed (on an amount), then after consummation or the husband's death, that agreed amount becomes binding. Mahr al-mithl is obliged only when nothing is agreed upon; here they later fixed an amount and the woman agreed, so mahr al-mithl is not obligatory; rather what was fixed is obligatory. [1786] (61) If he divorced her before intercourse and before seclusion, then she has mut'ah. The woman had no mahr specified; later they agreed on an amount. In such a case, if he divorces before intercourse or seclusion, then half of that amount is not due; rather she has mut'ah. Because at the time of marriage, no mahr was specified; later they specified an amount, but that specification does not make it as if mahr was specified from the beginning. So she gets mut'ah. The verse has passed: 'There is no blame upon you if you divorce women before you have touched them or specified for them an obligation. And provide for them...' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage clarifies the interplay between later agreement on mahr and pre-consummation divorce. The key point: if a man marries without specifying a mahr, and later the spouses agree on a specific mahr, that agreement is valid and binding upon consummation or death. However, if the husband divorces her before consummation or valid seclusion, she does not get half of that later-agreed mahr. Why? Because the original contract had no mahr specification; the later agreement does not retroactively become the original mahr. Therefore, the situation is treated as if no mahr was ever specified, and she is entitled to mut'ah under the Quranic verse (2:236). This is an important distinction: the later agreement is contingent upon consummation or death; if the marriage ends before that, the agreement has no effect, and the general rule of mut'ah applies.

Key Terms
تراضيا على تسمية مهر (taradaya 'ala tasmiyat mahr): Mutual agreement between spouses to fix a mahr amount after the marriage contract.

Increase in Mahr After the Marriage Contract
Ruling with qiyas on post-contract mahr increase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on post-contract mahr increases, distinguishing when the increase is binding and explaining the qiyas to sale.

Core Idea
A voluntary increase in mahr after marriage becomes binding upon consummation or death, like a price increase in a confirmed sale.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a husband voluntarily increases the mahr after the marriage contract. When is that increase binding? The Hanafi school uses qiyas (analogy) to sale to derive the ruling. We will unpack the conditions and the reasoning behind this unique fiqh ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a voluntary increase in mahr by the husband after the marriage contract. The ruling is that this increase becomes binding (lazim) upon the occurrence of either of two events.
2
Locate the conditions for binding
The passage states two conditions: either consummation of the marriage (dakhala biha) or death of either spouse (maata). These events confirm the marriage, making the increase obligatory.
If neither occurs (e.g., divorce before consummation), the increase is not binding.
3
Trace the qiyas analogy
The ruling is derived by analogizing mahr to a sale (bay'). In a sale, if the buyer voluntarily increases the price after the contract, the increase becomes binding once the sale is confirmed (e.g., upon delivery). Similarly, in marriage, the increase is binding upon consummation or death, which confirm the marital obligation.
The illa (effective cause) is that both mahr and price are financial obligations that can be voluntarily increased after contract, and the increase attaches to the obligation once it is finalized.
4
Note the hadith evidence
The author begins to cite a hadith from Abu Rafi' about the Prophet borrowing a young camel, which supports the permissibility of increasing mahr. The passage cuts off, but the hadith likely indicates that voluntary increases in financial obligations are valid.
The complete hadith is not given, but the qiyas remains the primary proof.
5
Evaluate the thamarah (practical consequence)
Practically, if a husband increases mahr but divorces before consummation, only half the original mahr is due, not the increase. This distinguishes post-contract increases from gifts, which are revocable.

The author begins to cite a hadith from Abu Rafi' about the Prophet borrowing a camel, but the passage is cut off at the page break. Ruling on Mutual Agreement on Mahr After Contract
Ruling on mahr when agreed after marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when spouses agree on a mahr amount after the marriage contract and identify when the agreed amount becomes binding.

Core Idea
If mahr is not fixed at marriage but later agreed, that agreement is binding upon consummation or death.

In this passage, we learn a crucial detail about mahr (dower) in Hanafi fiqh. Often, the mahr amount is specified at the time of marriage, but what if it is left unspecified? The text explains that if the spouses later mutually agree on a specific amount, that agreement becomes the binding mahr once the marriage is consummated or the husband dies. This clarifies the interplay between mutual consent and default rules like mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario is a marriage contract where no mahr was specified at the time of the contract.
This is a valid marriage in the Hanafi school; mahr is wajib but not a pillar.
2
Note the subsequent agreement
After the marriage, the spouses mutually agree on a specific mahr amount.
The agreement is a new specification of the mahr.
3
Determine when the agreed mahr becomes binding
The agreed mahr becomes binding upon either consummation of the marriage or the death of the husband. These two events trigger the full obligation.
The passage explicitly mentions these two conditions.
4
Contrast with mahr al-mithl
Mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is the default when no mahr is agreed. However, here a later agreement overrides that default.
The commentary confirms that mahr al-mithl applies only when nothing is fixed.
5
Understand the rationale
Mutual consent is respected; once the parties agree, that agreement is treated as if it were specified from the beginning for these outcomes.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of honoring post-contract agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهرا ثم تراضيا على تسمية مهر فهو لها ان دخل بها او مات عنها (۱۷۸۵) (۲۰) اگر عورت سے شادی کی اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں کیا پھر دونوں راضی ہو گئے مہر کی مقدار پر تو وہ اس کے لئے ہوگا اگر اس سے صحبت کی یا انتقال کر گیا۔ عورت سے شادی کی اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں کیا بعد میں دونوں کسی مقدار پر راضی ہو گئے تو صحبت کرنے کے بعد یا شوہر کے انتقال کے بعد وہی مہر لازم ہو گا جس پر دونوں راضی ہو گئے ہیں۔ مہر مثل اس وقت واجب ہوتا ہے جب کچھ بھی طے نہ ہو اور یہاں بعد میں ایک مقدار طے کر لی اور عورت اس پر راضی ہو گئی اس لئے مہر مثل لازم نہیں ہوگا بلکہ جو طے ہوا ہے وہی لازم ہوگا۔
And if he marries her and did not specify a mahr for her, then they mutually agree on specifying a mahr, then it is for her if he consummated with her or died. (20) If a man marries a woman and does not fix a mahr, then both agree on an amount, then that mahr will be for her if he consummated or died. After consummation or husband's death, the agreed mahr becomes binding. Mahr al-mithl is obligatory only when nothing is fixed; here an amount was fixed later, so mahr al-mithl is not binding, rather the agreed amount is binding.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This is a ruling on mahr (dower) when the amount is not specified at the time of marriage but is agreed upon later. The passage states that if a man marries a woman without specifying a mahr, and then both parties mutually agree on a specific amount, that agreed amount becomes the mahr due to the wife if consummation occurs or if the husband dies. The commentator clarifies that mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) is only applicable when no amount is fixed at all. Here, since an amount was later mutually agreed, that agreed amount takes precedence and becomes binding. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that mahr can be fixed after the contract by mutual consent, and once fixed, it is treated as the specified mahr.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower similar to that of women of her status when no mahr is specified.
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift obligatory upon the husband.

Mut'ah Upon Divorce Before Consummation Without Specified Mahr
Ruling on mut'ah for divorced woman with no specified mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah when mahr is not specified at the time of marriage, and explain why a later agreement does not count as specification for the purpose of half-mahr.

Core Idea
No specified mahr at contract means no half-mahr upon pre-consummation divorce; only mut'ah is wajib.

This lesson presents a nuanced ruling from Hanafi fiqh regarding the entitlement of a woman who is divorced before consummation (or valid seclusion) when the mahr was not fixed at the time of marriage, even if the couple later agreed on an amount. The core principle is that the later agreement does not retroactively change the legal status of the mahr for this particular scenario, so the wife receives mut'ah instead of half of the agreed sum. We will examine the ruling, its basis in the Quran, and the legal reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a marriage contract was concluded without specifying a mahr, the couple later agreed on a mahr amount, and then the husband divorces the wife before any consummation or valid seclusion (khalwah). Determine the key facts: no mahr at contract, post-contract agreement, divorce before physical intimacy.
Khalwah sahihah (valid seclusion) is treated like consummation in Hanafi law.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
In this scenario, the wife is entitled to mut'ah (a consolatory gift), not to half of the later-agreed mahr. Mut'ah is wajib (obligatory) on the husband. Understand the difference: if mahr had been specified at contract, half would be due upon pre-consummation divorce; since it was not, only mut'ah is due.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning
The later agreement on mahr is not considered a specification of mahr at the time of the contract. The ruling treats the case as if no mahr was ever fixed, because the condition for half-mahr (a specified mahr at the time of the contract) is absent. Therefore, the default rule for divorce before consummation without specified mahr applies: mut'ah.
This is an application of the Hanafi principle that rights are determined at the time of the contract, not by subsequent agreements.
4
Connect to the Quranic proof
The primary evidence is Quran 2:236, which explicitly prescribes mut'ah for women divorced before consummation when no mahr has been specified. The verse uses the imperative 'wamattioohunna' (and provide for them), indicating obligation. This verse applies directly to the scenario because the mahr was not specified at the time of divorce.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah according to Hanafi usul, yet the command is taken as wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها والخلوة فلها المتعة [۱۷۸۷ (۶۲) وان زاد في المهر بعد العقد لزمته الزيادة ان دخل بها او مات (۱۷۸۶) (۶۱) اگر اس کو طلاق دی صحبت سے پہلے اور خلوت سے پہلے تو اس کے لئے متعہ ہے۔ عورت کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں تھا۔ بعد میں کسی مقدار پر راضی ہو گئے ایسی صورت میں صحبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دے دی تو اس مقدار کا آدھا نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس کے لئے متعہ ہوگا۔ چونکہ نکاح کے وقت مہر متعین نہیں کیا بعد میں مقدار متعین کی ہے اس لئے اس متعینہ مقدار کا آدھا نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مہر متعین نہیں ہے اس لئے بغیر خلوت کے طلاق دی ہے تو اس کے لئے صرف متعہ ہو گا (۲) آیت گزر چکی ہے لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوا لهن فريضة ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره (الف) (آیت ۲۳۶ سورة البقرة ٢)
And if he divorces her before consummation and khalwah, then she gets mut'ah. (61) If he gives talaq before consummation and khalwah, then she gets mut'ah. The mahr was not fixed. Later they agreed on an amount. In such a case, if talaq is given before consummation or khalwah, then half of that amount is not due, rather mut'ah is due. Since no mahr was fixed at the time of marriage, and later an amount was fixed, half of that fixed amount is not due. It will be considered that mahr was not fixed, so due to talaq before khalwah, only mut'ah is due. Commentary
This lesson presents the ruling for mut'ah (consolatory gift) when a husband divorces his wife before consummation or valid seclusion (khalwah) and the mahr was not specified at the time of marriage, though it may have been agreed upon later. The passage explains that if the parties later agreed on a specific mahr amount, and then divorce occurs before consummation, the wife is not entitled to half of that agreed amount (as would be the case if mahr were specified at the contract). When a marriage contract lacks a specified mahr, any later agreement does not count as specification for the rule of half-mahr upon pre-consummation divorce; only mut'ah is wajib.

Increase in Mahr After Contract: Binding Upon Consummation or Death
Ruling on increase of mahr after the marriage contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an increase in mahr after the marriage contract and explain why it becomes binding upon consummation or death.

Core Idea
A voluntary increase in mahr after the contract becomes binding once the marriage is consummated or either spouse dies.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in marriage contracts: when a husband voluntarily increases the mahr after the nikah has been concluded. The key question is whether that increase is binding and when it becomes due. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on analogy and prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the husband increasing the mahr amount after the marriage contract. The ruling: the increase becomes wajib (binding) upon consummation or death.
This ruling applies to any voluntary increase by the husband.
2
Understand the condition for binding
The increase becomes binding only when the mahr becomes fully due: at consummation (dukhul) or upon the death of either spouse. Until then, the increase is a promise that can be revoked.
If the marriage ends before consummation (by divorce), the increase is not binding.
3
Examine the analogy to sale
The author compares mahr to a sale price. Just as a buyer can voluntarily increase the price in a sale, a husband can increase the mahr. This analogy shows the permissibility and binding nature of the increase.
The analogy is based on the similarity of exchange contracts.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of Abu Rafi' reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave an extra camel when repaying a debt, showing that giving extra is commendable and binding. By qiyas, increasing the mahr is similarly binding when it becomes due.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and is considered a valid proof.
5
Apply the principle
The increase is added to the original mahr and becomes part of the total mahr. Thus, the husband must pay the full amount (original + increase) upon consummation or death.
The same principle applies if the wife increases the mahr? The text only mentions the husband increasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان زاد في المهر بعد العقد لزمته الزيادة ان دخل بها او مات (۱۷۸۷) (۶۲) اور اگر زیادہ کیا مہر میں عقد کے بعد تو اس کو زیادتی لازم ہوگی اگر اس سے صحبت کی یا مر گیا۔ عقد کے وقت مثلا پانچ سو درہم مہر متعین کیا۔ بعد میں ایک سو اور زیادہ کر دیا۔ پس اگر صحبت کی یا محبت سے پہلے شوہر یا بیوی کا انتقال ہو گیا تو یہ ایک سو بھی لازم ہوگا۔ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ بعد میں جو کچھ زیادتی کرے وہ اصل مہر کے ساتھ شامل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے صحبت کی ہو یا انتقال کیا ہو تو زیادتی بھی لازم ہوگی (۲) مہر بیع کی طرح ہے۔ اور بیع میں مشتری شمن میں زیادتی کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے مہر میں بھی زیادتی کر سکتا ہے۔ یمن میں زیادتی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی رافع قال استسلف رسول الله الا الله بكرا فجائته ابل من الصدقة فامرني ان اقضى الرجل عنه ۱۷۸۸ (۶۳) وتسقط الزيادة بالطلاق قبل الدخول [۹] (۶۴) فان حطت من مهرها صح الحط ۱۹۰ (۶۵) واذا خلا الزوج بامرأته وليس هناك مانع من الوطئ بكره فقلت لم اجد في الابل الا جملا خيارا رباعيا فقال النبي الله اعطه اياه فان خيار الناس احسنهم قضاء (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی حسن القضاء ص ۱۹ انمبر ۳۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں حضور نے زیادہ دیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مہر بھی زیادہ دے سکتا ہے۔
And if he increases the mahr after the contract, the increase becomes binding if he consummates with her or dies. (62) If he increases the mahr after the contract, the increase becomes binding if he consummates or dies. For example, at the time of contract he fixed 500 dirhams, later he increased by 100. Then if he consummates or before intimacy either spouse dies, that 100 also becomes binding. The rule is that any increase after the contract is added to the original mahr. So if consummation or death occurs, the increase is also binding. (2) Mahr is like a sale. In a sale, the buyer can increase the price. So he can increase the mahr. The proof for increase is this hadith: From Abu Rafi', he said: The Messenger of Allah borrowed a young camel, then camels from sadaqah came to him, so he ordered me to repay the man. I said: I found nothing among the camels except a good four-year-old camel. The Prophet said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those who best repay debts. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Husn al-Qada, p. 19, no. 3346) In this hadith, the Prophet gave extra. From this, it is understood that the mahr can also be increased.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This ruling addresses an increase in mahr after the marriage contract has been finalized. The passage states that if the husband voluntarily increases the mahr amount after the contract, this increase becomes binding upon him if consummation takes place or if either the husband or wife dies. The commentator provides an example: if the mahr was originally 500 dirhams and the husband later adds 100 dirhams, then upon consummation or death, the full 600 dirhams is due. The principle is that any addition becomes part of the mahr. The commentator draws an analogy to a sale contract where the buyer can increase the price, and then cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave extra when repaying a debt, indicating that increasing a obligation is praiseworthy and binding.

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyadat): An increase in the mahr amount after the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately upon the husband's promise.
B) Upon consummation or the death of either spouse.
C) Only if the wife accepts it.
D) At the time of divorce.

Key Takeaway
A husband's voluntary increase in mahr after the marriage contract becomes a binding obligation upon consummation or death, and is not revocable after those events.

Increase in Mahr Cancelled by Divorce Before Consummation
Ruling on increase of mahr cancelled by divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increase of mahr upon divorce before consummation and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
An increase in mahr after the contract is cancelled upon divorce before consummation.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling regarding an increase in mahr (dower) after the marriage contract. If the husband divorces his wife before consummation, only half of the original mahr is due; any subsequent increase is cancelled. The proof is derived from the Quranic verse on divorce before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce before consummation when the mahr was increased after the contract. The ruling is that only half of the original mahr is wajib; the increase is cancelled.
This is a specific ruling within nikah and talaq.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:237, which mentions 'half of what you fixed' (نصف ما فرضتم).
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding the scope of 'fixed'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'what you fixed' (ما فرضتم) refers to the amount specified at the time of the contract, not later additions. Thus, only the original mahr is considered for the half obligation.
The increase is treated as a separate commitment.
4
Apply the ruling to an example
Original mahr 500 dirhams, later increase 100 dirhams. Divorce before consummation: half of original = 250 dirhams due; increase is cancelled.
Total due is 250 dirhams, not 300.

Source Text

Commentary
This lesson clarifies that if the husband increases the mahr after the marriage contract but then divorces his wife before consummation, the increase is cancelled. The increase after the contract is not considered part of that original specification, so it is not subject to the half rule.

Valid Khalwah Entitles Full Mahr Even Without Consummation
Ruling on effect of khalwah on mahr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which valid khalwah obligates full mahr in Hanafi fiqh and explain the qabd (possession) analogy.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, valid khalwah is legally equivalent to consummation for making the full mahr wajib.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling: a valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) between spouses, without any impediment to intercourse, obligates the full mahr if the marriage ends by divorce, even if actual intercourse did not occur. The passage presents the ruling and uses the analogy of a sale contract where the wife's surrender is like delivery. Understanding the precise conditions and the underlying analogy is essential for correctly applying the rule in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Determine the act (khalwah) and the condition that makes it legally effective: absence of any impediment to intercourse, such as menstruation, ihram, or presence of a third party.
The passage emphasizes 'no impediment' (la manna).
2
State the legal consequence
Upon divorce after valid khalwah, the full mahr becomes wajib. The husband must pay the entire specified mahr, even if he never had intercourse.
The passage explicitly mentions divorce as the triggering event.
3
Understand the qabd (possession) analogy
The commentator explains that the wife has surrendered herself (like goods in a sale) and the husband has effectively taken possession. His failure to consummate is his own negligence.
This reasoning roots the ruling in the concept of legal possession (qabd), not physical consummation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require actual consummation for full mahr. In Hanafi, khalwah suffices.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Imagine a couple who marry, have a private wedding night (khalwah) with no impediment, but then divorce before any physical contact. According to Hanafi, the wife is entitled to full mahr.
The husband cannot avoid mahr by a quick divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the husband secludes with his wife and there is no impediment to intercourse... (65) If the husband secludes with his wife and there is no impediment, then divorces her, the full mahr is due. The husband secludes with his wife but does not have intercourse, and there is no impediment to intercourse, then the full mahr becomes binding. The wife has surrendered the goods (herself) and the husband has effectively taken possession, so the full mahr is due. If the husband does not utilize (the right to intercourse), it is his negligence.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This final ruling addresses the effect of valid khalwah (seclusion) on the mahr obligation. The passage states that if a husband secludes himself with his wife in a manner that there is no legal or physical impediment to intercourse, then even if actual consummation does not occur, the full mahr becomes due upon divorce. The reasoning given by the commentator is that the wife has surrendered herself to the husband, and the husband has effectively taken possession (qabd) of that right, just as in a sale contract when goods are delivered. The failure to actually consummate is the husband's own negligence. This ruling emphasizes that khalwah sahihah is treated like actual consummation for the purpose of making the full mahr obligatory.

Key Terms
خلوت (khalwah): Valid seclusion between husband and wife with no impediment to intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the wife demands the mahr.

Key Takeaway
Valid khalwah with no impediment obligates the full mahr in Hanafi law, equating it with actual consummation.

Increase in Mahr Dropped by Pre-Consummation Divorce
Ruling on mahr increase dropped by pre-consummation divorce with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the increase in mahr when divorce occurs before consummation and justify it with the Quranic proof from al-Baqara 2:237.

Core Idea
Only the original mahr is halved upon pre-consummation divorce; any later increase is dropped.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a husband agrees to an increased mahr after the marriage contract but divorces his wife before consummation. Does the increase also get halved? The Hanafi school rules that only the original mahr is considered, drawing on the Quranic phrase 'half of what you specified.' Let's examine the proof and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce before consummation. The ruling is that the wife is entitled to half the mahr. But which mahr? The passage specifies that any increase after the contract is dropped.
This is a specific application of the general rule on half-mahr.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The author cites Quran 2:237: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them and you have already specified for them an obligation, then half of what you specified [is due].' The key phrase is 'half of what you specified' (نصف ما فرضتم).
The verse uses the past tense 'specified' (فرضتم), referring to the initial fixing of mahr at the contract.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'specified' (فرضتم) refers to the original determination made at the time of the marriage contract. Any subsequent increase (زيادة) is a separate transaction and is not included in 'what you specified' for the purpose of halving.
The increase is valid as a separate gift, but it does not become part of the original mahr obligation.
4
Apply the rule to the example
If the husband initially specified 500 dirhams and later added 100, the half-mahr upon pre-consummation divorce is 250 dirhams (half of 500), not 300 (half of 600). The increase is entirely dropped.
The hadith about the Prophet giving extra when repaying a debt is cited to show that increases are permissible, but it does not affect the half-mahr ruling.

Reduction of Mahr by the Wife is Valid
Ruling on wife's reduction of mahr with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a wife reducing her mahr and explain the Quranic basis for its validity.

Core Idea
The wife's reduction of mahr is valid because she owns it.

This short but crucial ruling affirms the wife's full ownership of her mahr. The Hanafi school, drawing on Quranic encouragement, holds that she may unilaterally reduce it without needing the husband's acceptance. Understanding this confirms her property rights in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its ruling
The wife reduces her specified mahr. The ruling is that this reduction is valid (sahih).
The act is called 'hatt' (reduction/remission).
2
Locate the basis of ownership
The mahr is the wife's exclusive property. Therefore, she has the right to waive part of it.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle: mahr is a debt owed to the wife.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Quran 2:237 says 'unless they forego' (إلا أن يعفون). This directly permits women to remit their mahr.
The verse encourages both parties to forego, but the woman's remission is highlighted.
4
Note the absence of condition
The ruling does not require the husband's acceptance or any special circumstance.
It is a unilateral right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

For if she reduces from her mahr, the reduction is valid. [1789] (64) So if the woman reduces from her mahr, the reduction is valid. This is presented as encouragement for women to reduce and for men to increase. The margin note 'khatt: kam karna' means 'chalk: reduction' likely indicating a marginal gloss. The ruling is straightforward: the wife's reduction is legally effective without requirement of acceptance.

Full Mahr Upon Valid Seclusion: Hanafi Position and Proofs
Ruling on full mahr due upon valid seclusion before divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mahr after valid seclusion and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the proofs for each.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) obligates full mahr in the Hanafi school — seclusion is equivalent to possession.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of valid seclusion on mahr before consummation. The Hanafi school holds that full mahr is due upon khulwa sahiha even without actual intercourse, while the Shafi'i school holds only half is due. We will explore the proofs from hadith, the athar of Umar (radiallahu anhu), and the opposing athar of Ibn Abbas (radiallahu anhu), and understand the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its context
Identify the act: valid seclusion followed by divorce before consummation. The Hanafi ruling is that full mahr is wajib. Understand that 'valid seclusion' means no legal or physical impediment to intercourse.
This ruling is based on the principle of possession and surrender of rights.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Look at the mursal hadith: 'Whoever uncovers a woman's veil and looks at her, the dower becomes obligatory, whether he has intercourse or not.' Also, the athar of Umar: 'If he closes the door and lowers the curtain, the dower becomes obligatory.' Note how these directly apply to seclusion.
The hadith uses the phrase 'فقد وجب الصداق' indicating immediate obligation, and 'دخل بها او لم يدخل' explicitly includes non-consummation.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only half mahr is due. His proof is the athar of Ibn Abbas: 'The dower does not become obligatory until he has intercourse with her; she gets half of it.' Identify the difference: Ibn Abbas requires actual intercourse for obligation.
The Shafi'i school considers seclusion insufficient for full mahr; only half is due because consummation did not occur.
4
Compare the two proofs
Evaluate the strength: The Hanafi proofs include a direct hadith (though mursal) and an athar from Umar, a caliph. The Shafi'i proof is an athar from Ibn Abbas. Understand the Hanafi response: the hadith and Umar's athar are stronger; seclusion is analogous to possession.
Hanafi usul accepts mursal hadith under certain conditions. The athar of Umar is preferred over Ibn Abbas due to Umar's position and the fact that his statement covers 'iddah and inheritance as well.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: a woman divorced after valid seclusion receives full mahr in Hanafi school, half in Shafi'i. Identify that the Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by the majority of Companions' practice and the hadith.
This difference can affect financial outcomes significantly; hence it is essential for a mufti to know the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا خلا الزوج بامرأته وليس هناك مانع من الوطئ ثم طلقها فلها كمال مهرها [۱۷۹۰] (۶۵) اگر خلوت کرے شوہر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ اور وہاں ولی سے کوئی مانع نہ ہو پھر اس کو طلاق دے تو اس کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ ا شوہر اپنی بیوی سے خلوت کرے لیکن وطی نہ کرے اور وہاں وطی کرنے سے کوئی مانع نہ ہو تو پورا مہر لازم ہو جائے گا۔ عورت نے مال سپرد کر دیا اور گویا کہ شوہر نے قبضہ کر لیا اس لئے پورا مہر لازم ہوگا۔ اب شوہر اس کو استعمال نہ کرے تو یہ اس کی کوتاہی ہے حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جو ان اونٹ قرض لیا۔ پس آپ کے پاس صدقے کا اونٹ آیا تو مجھ کو حکم دیا کہ میں جوان اونٹ ادا کروں۔ میں نے کہا نہیں پاتا ہوں مگر اعلی اونٹ چار دانت والا، آپ نے فرمایا وہی اس کو دے دو۔ اس لئے کہ اچھے لوگ وہ ہیں جو اچھے انداز میں قرض ادا کرے ( ب ) اگر عورت کو طلاق دے دو اس کو چھونے سے پہلے اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا ہے تو جتنا متعین کیا ہے اس کا آدھا ہو گا (ج) اگر تم عورتوں کو طلاق دے دو اس کو چھونے سے پہلے اور تم نے اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا ہے تو جتنا متعین کیا ہے اس کا آدھا ہوگا۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ معاف کر دیں۔ یا وہ شخص کچھ زیادہ کر دے جس کے ہاتھ میں نکاح کا عقد ہے ( یعنی شوہر ) اور اگر وہ (عورت) معاف کر دے تو یہ تقوی کے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ ثم طلقها فلها كمال مهرها) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن ثوبان قال قال رسول الله الله من كشف خمار امرأة ونظر اليها فقد وجب الصداق دخل بها او لم يدخل بها (الف) (دار قطنی، كتاب النكاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۳۷۸۰ رسن للبیہقی ، باب من قال من الغلق بابا اوارخی ستر افقد وجب الصداق ج، سابع ص ۴۱۸ نمبر ۷ (۱۳۴۸) (۳) اثر میں بھی ہے قال عمر بن الخطاب اذا اغلق بابا وارخى سترا فقد وجب لها الصداق وعليها العدة ولها الميراث (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۳۷۷۹ سفن اللبیہقی ، باب من قال من اغلاق بابا اوارخی سترا فقد وجب الصداق ج سابع ص ۴۱۶، نمبر (۱۴۴۸) اس اثر اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلوت صحیحہ ہو جائے تو مہر کامل لازم ہو جائے گا چاہے صحبت نہ کی ہو۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ عورت کے لئے آدھا مہر ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل ابن عباس کا اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لا يجب الصداق حتى يجامعها، لها نصفه (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب وجوب الصداق ج سادس ص ۲۹۰ نمبر ۱۰۸۸۲)
And if the husband secludes himself with his wife and there is no impediment to intercourse, then divorces her, she gets her full mahr. [1790] (65) If the husband secludes himself with his wife and there is no impediment from the guardian, then he divorces her, she gets full mahr. The husband secludes with his wife but does not have intercourse, and there is no impediment to intercourse, then full mahr becomes due. The woman has handed over the property, as if the husband has taken possession, so full mahr is due. If the husband does not use it, it is his negligence. Footnote: (a) The Prophet took a camel loan... he said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those who best repay. (b) If you divorce women before touching them and have specified mahr, then half of what was specified is due. (c) If you divorce women before touching them and have specified mahr, then half of what was specified is due, unless they remit or the one in whose hand is the marriage contract remits. And to remit is nearer to piety. Then he divorced her, she gets her full mahr. A mursal hadith: From Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever uncovers a woman's veil and looks at her, the dower becomes obligatory, whether he has intercourse with her or not. (a) (Darqutni, etc.) Also an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: If he closes the door and lowers the curtain, the dower becomes obligatory for her, and she must observe 'iddah, and she inherits. (b) From this hadith and athar it is known that if valid seclusion occurs, full mahr becomes due even without intercourse. Imam al-Shafi'i says that she gets half mahr. His proof is the athar of Ibn Abbas: Ibn Abbas said: The dower does not become obligatory until he has intercourse with her; she gets half of it. (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, etc.)
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling on the effect of valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) on mahr when divorce occurs before consummation. The Hanafi position is that if the husband secludes with his wife with no impediment to intercourse and then divorces her, full mahr is due. The reasoning is that the wife has surrendered herself and the husband has taken effective possession; if he does not consummate, it is his own fault. The author supports this with a mursal hadith that looking with uncovered veil obligates mahr, and with the athar of Umar that closing the door and lowering the curtain obligates mahr, 'iddah, and inheritance. Then an inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only half mahr is due, adducing an athar from Ibn Abbas that mahr is not obligatory until actual intercourse occurs. The Hanafi response is implicit in the proofs: seclusion itself is sufficient to complete the exchange of rights. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the proofs, then the opposing view.

Key Terms
خلوة صحیحہ (khulwa sahiha): Valid seclusion where the husband and wife are alone in a place where intercourse is possible and there is no legal or physical impediment.
صداق (sadaq): The dowry or mahr, synonymous with mahr in this context.
اثر (athar): A saying or action of a Companion, here used as a proof alongside hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half mahr
B) Full mahr
C) No mahr
D) An amount determined by a judge

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) triggers full mahr exactly like intercourse, because possession has been established.

Impediments to Valid Seclusion and Half Mahr
Listing impediments that invalidate seclusion and reduce mahr to half.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four impediments that invalidate seclusion and apply the ruling that half mahr becomes wajib upon divorce in such cases.

Core Idea
Seclusion with an impediment to intercourse is invalid, reducing mahr to half upon divorce.

Valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) is a key concept in Hanafi marriage law: it triggers the obligation of full mahr if followed by divorce. However, the law recognizes that certain physical and ritual conditions make intercourse impossible or forbidden. The author enumerates four such impediments: sickness, fasting in Ramadan, ihram, and menstruation. Understanding these exceptions is essential for correctly determining the mahr owed.

Guided Path
1
List the four impediments
Read the passage and identify each impediment: sickness, fasting in Ramadan, ihram for Hajj/Umrah, and menstruation.
Note that both husband and wife could be subject to the first three; menstruation applies only to the wife.
2
Understand why each invalidates seclusion
For each impediment, explain why intercourse is not possible or prohibited: sickness removes desire; fasting in Ramadan makes intercourse a sin requiring kaffarah; ihram makes intercourse a sin requiring dam; menstruation makes intercourse absolutely prohibited.
The common thread is that the wife is not considered to have fully submitted herself, so full seclusion is not achieved.
3
Apply the ruling of half mahr
If divorce occurs after an invalid seclusion, only half the specified mahr is wajib. This parallels the rule for divorce before any seclusion.
The ruling is based on qiyas: the impediment prevents the effect of seclusion, so the mahr is reduced as if no seclusion occurred.
4
Recognize the rational basis
The passage uses rational inference (dalil aqli): since intercourse is impossible or forbidden, the seclusion cannot be considered complete, and the wife has not truly submitted.
This is not based on direct textual evidence but on logical deduction from the purpose of seclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان احدهما مريضا او صائما في رمضان او محرما بحج او عمرة او كانت حائضا فليست بخلوة صحيحة ولو طلقها فيجب نصف المهر [۱۷۹۱] (۶۶) اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک بیمار ہو یا رمضان میں روزہ ہو یا حج یا عمرہ کا محرم ہو یا حائضہ ہو تو یہ خلوت صحیحہ نہیں اگر طلاق دیدی تو آدھا مہر واجب ہوگا۔ ان چیزوں کے ہوتے ہوئے آدمی صحبت نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے پوری خلوت نہیں ہوئی ۔ اور عورت کی جانب سے مال سپرد کرنا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے پورا مہر لازم نہیں ہوگا ۔ مثلا بیمار ہو تو رغبت نہیں ہوگی۔ اور رمضان کا روزہ ہو تو صحبت کرنے سے کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور احرام ہو تو صحبت کرنے سے دم لازم ہو گا۔ اور حائضہ ہو تو صحبت ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے ان چیزوں سے خلوت صحیحہ نہیں ہوئی۔
And if one of them is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or in ihram for Hajj or Umrah, or she is menstruating, then it is not a valid seclusion; and if he divorces her, then half the mahr is due. [1791] (66) And if one of them is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or in ihram for Hajj or Umrah, or she is menstruating, then this is not a valid seclusion; if he divorces, half the mahr will be obligatory. Because with these conditions, a man cannot have intercourse, so complete seclusion has not occurred. And the woman's act of surrendering property has not been effectuated, so full mahr is not due. For example, if sick, there is no desire; if fasting in Ramadan, intercourse would necessitate kaffarah; if in ihram, intercourse would necessitate dam; if she is menstruating, intercourse is prohibited. Therefore, these conditions prevent valid seclusion.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage lists conditions that invalidate seclusion (khulwa) and thus reduce the mahr to half if divorce occurs before consummation. The author states that if either the husband or wife has a legal or physical impediment to intercourse, the seclusion is not considered valid. The list includes: sickness, fasting in Ramadan, being in ihram for Hajj or Umrah, and menstruation. The reasoning is that in each case, intercourse is either prohibited (haram) or not feasible, so the wife has not truly surrendered herself, and the husband cannot be said to have control. Therefore, only half mahr is due, as in the general rule for pre-consummation divorce. The commentary gives specific examples: a sick person lacks desire; a fasting person would need to pay kaffarah; a pilgrim in ihram would have to perform dam; and a menstruating woman is prohibited from intercourse. The ruling is based on rational inference (qiyas) from the general principle that seclusion must be free of impediments.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khulwa sahiha): Valid seclusion with no impediment to intercourse; here defined negatively by the absence of such impediments.
مانع (mani'): An impediment, either physical (sickness) or legal (fasting, ihram, menstruation) that prevents intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full mahr
B) Half mahr
C) No mahr
D) Mahr is determined by the wife

Key Takeaway
When an impediment to intercourse is present during seclusion, the seclusion is invalid and upon divorce only half mahr is wajib.

Full Mahr for Seclusion by a Man Unable to Consummate
Ruling on full mahr when a man with no penis secludes with his wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a husband with severed genitals secludes with his wife, and explain the proof from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Seclusion obligates full mahr even if the husband cannot physically consummate.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi fiqh: a man whose penis has been severed (majbub) secludes with his wife and then divorces. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, full mahr is due. The ruling is based on the principle that valid seclusion itself triggers the obligation, supported by a mursal hadith and the practice of Umar. Understanding this ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school applies the general rule of khulwa sahiha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The husband is a majbub (severed penis) who cannot physically consummate. He performs valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) with his wife and then divorces her.
The case is specific to physical inability, but the principle extends to any situation where seclusion occurs without consummation.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Full mahr is wajib upon the husband according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The wife is entitled to the entire mahr, not half.
This is the position from the Zahir al-Riwayah, implying it is the mufta bihi.
3
Identify the proof
The author cites a mursal hadith from al-Daraqutni: 'Whoever uncovers a woman's veil and looks at her, the dower becomes obligatory, whether he has intercourse with her or not.' Also an athar from Umar: 'If he closes the door and lowers the curtain, the dower becomes obligatory.'
Both proofs indicate that seclusion alone, not intercourse, triggers full mahr.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly says 'dakhala biha aw lam dakhul' — whether he enters or not — so inability to consummate is irrelevant. The athar defines seclusion by closing door and lowering curtain.
The mursal hadith is zanni al-thubut but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for non-criminal matters.
5
Note the intra-madhhab context
The text presents only Abu Hanifa's view, implying it is the relied-upon position. No dissent from the Sahibayn is recorded here.
This ruling may be contested by other schools that require actual intercourse for full mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا خلا المجبوب بامرأته ثم طلقها فلها كمال المهر عند [۱۷۹۲] (۲۷) اگر خلوت کی ذکر کئے ہوئے آدمی نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ پھر اس کو طلاق دی تو اس کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ ذکر کٹا ہوا ہے ایسا آدمی بیوی کے ساتھ صحبت نہیں کر سکتا اس کے باوجود اگر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ خلوت صحیحہ کی تو اس پر پورا مہر لازم ہوگا۔ عورت نے اپنا مال سپرد کر دیا۔ یہ اور بات ہے کہ مرد کی مجبوری کی وجہ سے وہ وصول نہیں کر پا رہا ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر پورا مہر لازم ہوگا (۲) اوپر میں دار قطنی کی حدیث دخل بها او لم يدخل بها (دار قطنی نمبر ۳۷۸۰) سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے کہ صحبت نہ کر سکے تب بھی حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن ثوبان قال قال رسول الله الله من كشف خمار امرأة ونظر اليها فقد وجب الصداق دخل بها او لم يدخل بها (الف) (دار قطنی، كتاب النكاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۳۷۸۰ رسن للبیہقی ، باب من قال من الغلق بابا اوارخی ستر افقد وجب الصداق ج، سابع ص ۴۱۸ نمبر ۷ (۱۳۴۸) (۳) اثر میں بھی ہے قال عمر بن الخطاب اذا اغلق بابا وارخى سترا فقد وجب لها الصداق وعليها العدة ولها الميراث (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۳۷۷۹ سفن اللبیہقی ، باب من قال من اغلاق بابا اوارخی سترا فقد وجب الصداق ج سابع ص ۴۱۶، نمبر (۱۴۴۸) اس اثر اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلوت صحیحہ ہو جائے تو مہر کامل لازم ہو جائے گا چاہے صحبت نہ کی ہو۔
And if the man with severed genitals (majbub) secludes with his wife and then divorces her, she gets her full mahr according to [Abu Hanifa]. [1792] (27) If a man who has had his genitals severed secludes with his wife and then divorces her, she gets full mahr according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The man whose genitals are cut cannot have intercourse with his wife; nevertheless, if he performed valid seclusion with his wife, full mahr is due. The woman has surrendered her property. It is another matter that due to the man's inability he cannot take possession. So full mahr is due. (2) The hadith of al-Daraqutni 'whether he has intercourse or not' (no. 3780) also supports that even if he cannot have intercourse, still: A mursal hadith: From Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever uncovers a woman's veil and looks at her, the dower becomes obligatory, whether he has intercourse with her or not. (a) (al-Daraqutni, etc.) Also an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: If he closes the door and lowers the curtain, the dower becomes obligatory for her, and she must observe 'iddah, and she inherits. (b) (al-Daraqutni, etc.) From this hadith and athar it is known that if valid seclusion occurs, full mahr becomes due even without intercourse.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific case: a man who is majbub (his penis has been severed) and thus cannot physically consummate the marriage. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if such a man secludes with his wife (khulwa sahiha) and then divorces her, full mahr is due. The reasoning is that the wife has surrendered herself, and the husband's inability to consummate does not negate the validity of seclusion; it is his own failing. The author supports this with the same mursal hadith and the athar of Umar that were cited earlier: seclusion itself obligates full mahr, whether intercourse occurs or not. This ruling shows that the Hanafi school treats seclusion as equivalent to actual consummation for the purpose of mahr, even when the husband is physically incapable. The text notes that Abu Hanifa's view is the reference ('ind), implying it is the operative position.

Key Terms
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis has been severed, rendering him incapable of intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what mahr is due if a man who is majbub (lacks penis) secludes with his wife and then divorces her?
A) Half mahr
B) No mahr
C) Full mahr
D) Mahr is discretionary

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khulwa sahiha) triggers full mahr obligation, regardless of the husband's ability to consummate.

Hanafi Ruling on Valid Seclusion and Its Exceptions
Ruling and conditions for valid seclusion effect on mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khalwah sahihah and identify the exceptions that prevent full mahr.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion triggers full mahr; but if intercourse is legally impossible, only half mahr is due.

This lesson explains the Hanafi position that valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) between spouses entitles the wife to full mahr upon divorce, even without intercourse. However, certain impediments—sickness, fasting in Ramadan, ihram, or menstruation—prevent seclusion from being valid, resulting in only half mahr. We will explore the evidence and reasoning behind these rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the first part of the passage: if a husband divorces his wife after valid seclusion, she receives full mahr.
This is the default rule.
2
Locate the dalil
Review the mursal hadith and the athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab that support the rule.
These proofs establish seclusion as equivalent to consummation.
3
List the exceptions
Note the four conditions that invalidate seclusion: sickness, Ramadan fasting, ihram, and menstruation.
These make intercourse impossible or prohibited.
4
Understand the reasoning
In these exceptions, the woman's complete surrender (taslim) is not achieved, so only half mahr is due.
The impediment prevents full financial obligation.

كتاب النكاح
ثم طلقها فلها كمال مهرها ) وان كان احدهما مريضا او صائما في رمضان او محرما بحج او عمرة او كانت حائضا فليست بخلوة صحيحة ولو طلقها فيجب نصف المهر ( ۲۲ ) حدیث مرسل میں ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن ثوبان قال قال رسول الله الله من كشف خمار امرأة ونظر اليها فقد وجب الصداق دخل بها او لم يدخل بها (الف) (دار قطنی، كتاب النكاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۳۷۸۰ رسن للبیهقی ، باب من قال من الغلق بابا اوارخی ستر افقد وجب الصداق ج، سابع ص ۴۱۸ نمبر ۷ (۱۳۴۸) (۳) اثر میں بھی ہے قال عمر بن الخطاب اذا اغلق بابا وارخى سترا فقد وجب لها الصداق وعليها العدة ولها الميراث (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۳۷۷۹ سفن اللبیہقی ، باب من قال من اغلاق بابا اوارخی سترا فقد وجب الصداق ج سابع ص ۴۱۶، نمبر (۱۴۴۸) اس اثر اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلوت صحیحہ ہو جائے تو مہر کامل لازم ہو جائے گا چاہے صحبت نہ کی ہو۔
امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ عورت کے لئے آدھا مہر ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل ابن عباس کا اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لا يجب الصداق حتى يجامعها، لها نصفه (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب وجوب الصداق ج سادس ص ۲۹۰ نمبر ۱۰۸۸۲) [۱۷۹۱] (۶۶) اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک بیمار ہو یا رمضان میں روزہ ہو یا حج یا عمرہ کا محرم ہو یا حائضہ ہو تو یہ خلوت صحیحہ نہیں اگر طلاق دیدی تو آدھا مہر واجب ہوگا۔
ان چیزوں کے ہوتے ہوئے آدمی صحبت نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے پوری خلوت نہیں ہوئی ۔ اور عورت کی جانب سے مال سپرد کرنا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے پورا مہر لازم نہیں ہوگا ۔ مثلا بیمار ہو تو رغبت نہیں ہوگی۔ اور رمضان کا روزہ ہو تو صحبت کرنے سے کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور احرام ہو تو صحبت کرنے سے دم لازم ہو گا۔ اور حائضہ ہو تو صحبت ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے ان چیزوں سے خلوت صحیحہ نہیں ہوئی۔
Then he divorces her, so she has her full mahr. And if one of them is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or a muhrim for Hajj or Umrah, or she is menstruating, then it is not a valid seclusion, and if he divorces her, half the mahr is obligatory. (22) There is a mursal hadith: from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever uncovers a woman's khimar and looks at her, then the sadaq is obligatory, whether he enters her or does not enter her.' (a) (Darqutni, Kitab al-Nikah vol. 3 p.213 no.3780; Baihaqi, Bab man qala...). Also there is an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'If he closes a door and draws a curtain, then the sadaq is obligatory for her, and she has the iddah, and she has the inheritance.' (b) (Darqutni...). This athar and hadith show that if valid seclusion occurs, then full mahr becomes obligatory even if intercourse did not occur. Imam Shafi'i says that she has half the mahr. His evidence is the athar of Ibn Abbas: 'The sadaq is not obligatory until he has intercourse with her; she has half of it.' (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...). (66) And if one of them is sick, or fasting in Ramadan, or a muhrim for Hajj or Umrah, or a menstruating woman, then this is not valid seclusion; if he divorces, half the mahr is wajib. Because when these conditions exist, a man cannot have intercourse, so complete seclusion has not occurred. And the woman's delivery of property (herself) has not been found, so full mahr is not necessary. For example, if sick, there is no desire; if fasting in Ramadan, then intercourse would require kaffarah; if in ihram, then intercourse would require dam; if menstruating, intercourse is prohibited. Therefore, these conditions do not constitute valid seclusion.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri discusses the legal effect of valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) on the obligation of mahr upon divorce. The Hanafi position, based on a mursal hadith and an athar of Umar, holds that once a man and woman are lawfully secluded in a manner where intercourse is possible, full mahr becomes due upon divorce even without actual intercourse. This is because seclusion is considered a de facto consummation regarding financial rights. The Shafi'i school, relying on an athar of Ibn Abbas, argues that only half mahr is due because actual intercourse is required for full mahr. The Hanafi response is that the athar of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as referring to the completion of the obligation; seclusion is equivalent to intercourse in establishing full mahr because the woman has completely surrendered herself. However, the general rule has exceptions: if either party has a legal or physical impediment to intercourse (sickness, fasting in Ramadan, ihram, or menstruation), seclusion is not considered valid, and only half the mahr is due upon divorce because the woman's delivery of herself is incomplete.

Key Terms
خلوة صحيحة (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion between a married couple without witnesses where nothing prevents intercourse.
مهر (mahr): The dower paid by husband to wife as obligatory consideration in marriage.
متعة (mut'ah): A gift given to a divorced woman as compensation, especially when no mahr was specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an exception that invalidates khalwah sahihah according to the passage?
A) The husband is sick.
B) The wife is fasting in Ramadan.
C) The husband is in ihram for Umrah.
D) The wife is in her iddah from a previous marriage.

Key Takeaway
Valid seclusion obligates full mahr; exceptions (sickness, fasting, ihram, menstruation) reduce it to half.

Inter-Madhhab Dispute: Khalwah Sahihah and Mahr
Inter-madhhab dispute on mahr after seclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on mahr after seclusion and analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence.

Core Idea
Hanafi says full mahr due to seclusion; Shafi'i says half; the difference stems from conflicting athars.

This lesson presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the effect of valid seclusion on mahr. After stating the Hanafi rule and evidence, the text introduces Imam al-Shafi'i's objection based on an athar of Ibn Abbas. We will examine both proofs, the Hanafi rebuttal, and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Recall from the previous lesson: full mahr is due after valid seclusion.
This is the default ruling.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only half mahr is due because seclusion does not substitute for intercourse.
His evidence is the athar of Ibn Abbas.
3
Compare the proofs
Hanafi uses a mursal hadith and Umar's athar; Shafi'i uses Ibn Abbas's athar.
The conflict is between different sahih transmissions.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets Ibn Abbas's athar to mean completion of obligation, not its initial establishment. Seclusion is legally equivalent to intercourse due to the woman's full surrender.
This rebuttal is based on istihsan and consideration of intent.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, under Hanafi the wife gets full mahr; under Shafi'i she gets half.
This affects financial planning in marriage contracts.
