Conditions in Marriage: Effect of Violation on Mahr
Ruling on marriage with a condition and its violation effect on mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a marriage condition is violated and explain the shift from named mahr to mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A valid condition in marriage is binding; violation shifts the mahr to mahr al-mithl.

In Hanafi fiqh, marriage contracts often include conditions beneficial to the spouses. This lesson examines a case where the wife stipulates that her husband neither move her from her city nor marry another wife over her. The central question: what happens to the mahr if the husband violates the condition? The answer distinguishes between honoring and breaking the condition, with significant financial consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a marriage contract with a valid condition. The ruling is that the contract is sahih and the condition is binding.
The condition does not contradict the essence of nikah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'Al-muslimuna 'ala shurutihim' (Muslims are bound by their conditions).
This is a general principle applicable to all contracts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes that any condition agreed upon in a contract must be fulfilled. Here, the wife agreed to a specific mahr only on condition of the husband's promise.
When the husband breaks the condition, the wife's consent to the specific mahr is no longer valid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers such conditions invalid because they restrict the husband's rights; the marriage is valid but the condition is void.
Hanafi positions uphold the condition, leading to different mahr outcomes.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi: if condition broken, mahr al-mithl. Shafi'i: condition void, so named mahr remains due.
Practical difference in financial entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوج امرأة على الف درهم على ان لا يخرجها من البلد او على ان لا يتزوج عليها امرأة فان وفى بالشرط فلها المسمى 
 وان تزوج عليها او اخرجها من البلد فلها مهر مثلها 
 عورت نے ایک ہزار مہر کے بدلے شادی کی اس شرط پر کہ اس کو شہر سے نہیں نکالے گا۔ یا اس شرط پر کہ اس عورت کے بعد دوسری عورت سے شادی نہیں کرے گا۔ پس اگر اس شرط کو پوری کی تو جتنا مہر متعین کیا ہے وہ مل جائے گا یعنی اس کو ایک ہزار درہم مل جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے شرط پوری کر دی۔ المسلمون عند شروطهم. 
 شرط تو یہی تھی کہ اس پر دوسری عورت سے شادی نہیں کرے گا یا شہر سے نہیں نکالے گا۔ لیکن شوہر نے ان شرطوں کو پوری نہیں کی ۔ بلکہ اس کے اوپر دوسری عورت سے شادی کر لی یا اس کو شہر سے نکالا تو اب عورت کے لئے مہر سمی نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مہر مثل ہوگا۔ شرط پوری کرنے پر ایک ہزار پر راضی ہوئی تھی۔ شرط پوری نہیں کی تو ایک ہزار پر راضی نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لئے اب اس کے لئے معیار مبرشل ہوگا کیونکہ گویا کہ مہر ہی متعین نہیں ہوا۔
And if a woman marries a man for one thousand dirhams on condition that he does not take her out of the city or that he does not marry another woman over her, then if he fulfills the condition, she gets the named (mahr). And if he marries another over her or takes her out of the city, then she gets mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). ... The woman married for one thousand mahr on the condition that he would not take her out of the city, or on the condition that he would not marry another woman after her. So if he fulfills the condition, he gets the specified mahr, i.e., she gets one thousand dirhams, because the husband fulfilled the condition. 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' The condition was that he would not marry another woman or take her out of the city. But the husband did not fulfill these conditions; rather, he married another woman over her or took her out of the city. Now the woman does not get the named mahr but gets mahr al-mithl. She agreed to the one thousand on condition that it be fulfilled; since it was not fulfilled, she is not pleased with the one thousand. Therefore, the benchmark for her is mahr al-mithl, as if the mahr was not specified.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage deals with a marriage contract that includes a condition (shart) stipulated by the wife: either that the husband will not move her from her city or that he will not marry a second wife over her. The ruling is: if the husband honors the condition, the wife is entitled to the mahr that was specified in the contract (here, one thousand dirhams). If he violates the condition, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the customary mahr for a woman of her status). The reasoning is that the wife only agreed to the specific mahr in exchange for the condition; if the condition is broken, her consent is no longer valid, so the mahr reverts to what is customary, as if no specific mahr was agreed. The commentary cites the general principle 'al-muslimuna 'ala shurutihim' (Muslims are bound by their conditions), which is a well-known hadith. This illustrates the Hanafi approach to conditions in marriage: conditions that do not contradict the object of the contract are valid and must be observed; violation may affect the mahr.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary mahr given to a woman of similar status to the bride (similar age, beauty, wealth, etc.), used when the specified mahr becomes invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The named mahr
B) Half of the named mahr
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) No mahr because she agreed

Key Takeaway
A valid condition in marriage is binding; breaking it converts the mahr to mahr al-mithl, not invalidating the marriage.

Master's Obligation for Slave's Marriage
Ruling with proof on master's duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding a master's duty to provide housing for his slave woman after her marriage, and identify the proof (athar) used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A master is not obliged to house his married slave woman or facilitate conjugal visits; her service to him takes precedence over the husband's right.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the marriage of a slave woman. When a master marries off his female slave, is he required to provide a home for the husband or allow her to stay overnight? The text clarifies that the master's ownership rights override the husband's conjugal rights, and the slave woman continues to serve her master. The proof is drawn from a statement of Ibn Umar regarding the liability for mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the master marrying off his slave woman. The ruling is that he is not obliged to provide a house for the husband or to let her stay overnight with him.
The Arabic phrase 'ليس عليه ان يبوئها بيتا' directly negates any obligation.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is an athar (narration) from Ibn Umar stating that the mahr is upon the one who gives in marriage (the father for a free daughter, the master for a slave). This establishes that the financial responsibility of marriage lies with the husband or the slave himself, not the master.
The athar is referenced from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Analyze the proof's implication
Since the mahr is a liability on the slave (or the husband), the master is not burdened with marital expenses. By extension, he is not required to provide housing or facilitate cohabitation, as these are not his obligations.
The master's ownership of the slave woman's service remains intact.
4
Note the underlying principle
The principle is that the master's right of ownership (service and property) takes precedence over the husband's right to her private part. The husband's claim is limited, so the master may keep her in service and only allow access when convenient.
This is a unique Hanafi position emphasizing ownership rights.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, the husband has no right to demand overnight stays or a separate residence. He must coordinate with the master for opportunities to meet his wife. If he cannot, he has no legal recourse against the master.
The slave woman continues to live and work in the master's house.

Its proof is this athar: Ibn Umar said: The mahr is upon whom you have married off, meaning the mahr is upon the son (Reference). Commentary
This passage contains a ruling (hukm) from the Hanafi school regarding the marriage of a slave woman owned by a master. The base text (matn) states: when a master marries off his slave woman, he is not obliged to provide a house for the husband or to allow her to stay overnight with him. This establishes that the mahr is a liability on the slave himself, not the master, and the slave can be sold to pay it. The key principle is that the master's right of ownership overrides the husband's conjugal rights, so there is no obligation to facilitate cohabitation beyond allowing access when possible.

Marriage with Conditions on Travel and Polygyny
Rulings on conditional marriage stipulations regarding residence and polygyny

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional mahr and identify when it changes to mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A marriage condition binding mahr: fulfill the condition, pay the specified mahr; break it, pay mahr al-mithl.

In Hanafi fiqh, marriage contracts can include valid conditions that affect the mahr obligation. This passage presents two clear rulings: if a husband fulfills a condition (e.g., not taking his wife out of the city or not marrying another), the specified mahr is due. If he breaches the condition, the mahr becomes mahr al-mithl. This lesson dissects the ruling and its underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a marriage contract with a condition attached to the mahr. Identify the two scenarios: condition fulfilled vs. breached.
The condition must be valid (not contrary to Shariah).
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario 1: Husband fulfills condition → wife gets specified mahr (musamma). Scenario 2: Husband breaches condition → wife gets mahr al-mithl.
The breach can be marrying another woman or taking her out of the city.
3
Trace the legal reasoning
The woman consented to the specified mahr only with the condition. If the condition is broken, her consent is no longer valid for that amount, so it reverts to mahr al-mithl as if no mahr was specified.
This is based on the principle that Muslims are bound by their conditions (al-muslimoon 'ala shurootihim).
4
Note the underlying principle
The principle 'al-muslimoon 'ala shurootihim' validates such conditions and makes them enforceable, affecting the mahr.
The condition must not contradict the essence of marriage.

Source Text

[۱۸۰۱] (۷۶) اگر شادی کی عورت نے ایک ہزار پر اس شرط پر کہ اس کو شہر سے نہیں نکالے گا یا اس شرط پر کہ اس پر دوسری عورت سے شادی نہیں کرے گا۔ پس اگر شرط پوری کی تو عورت کو مہر متعین ملے گا۔ عورت نے ایک ہزار مہر کے بدلے شادی کی اس شرط پر کہ اس کو شہر سے نہیں نکالے گا۔ یا اس شرط پر کہ اس عورت کے بعد دوسری عورت سے شادی نہیں کرے گا۔ پس اگر اس شرط کو پوری کی تو جتنا مہر متعین کیا ہے وہ مل جائے گا یعنی اس کو ایک ہزار درہم مل جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے شرط پوری کر دی۔ المسلمون عند شروطهم. [۱۸۰۲ (۷۷) اور اگر اس پر دوسری عورت سے شادی کی یا اس کو شہر سے نکالا تو اس کے لئے مہر مثل ہوگا۔ شرط تو یہی تھی کہ اس پر دوسری عورت سے شادی نہیں کرے گا یا شہر سے نہیں نکالے گا۔ لیکن شوہر نے ان شرطوں کو پوری نہیں کی ۔ بلکہ اس کے اوپر دوسری عورت سے شادی کر لی یا اس کو شہر سے نکالا تو اب عورت کے لئے مہر سمی نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مہر مثل ہوگا۔ شرط پوری کرنے پر ایک ہزار پر راضی ہوئی تھی۔ شرط پوری نہیں کی تو ایک ہزار پر راضی نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لئے اب اس کے لئے معیار مبرشل ہوگا کیونکہ گویا کہ مہر ہی متعین نہیں ہوا۔ حاشیه : (ب) حضرت ابن عمر نے فرمایا مہر اس پر ہے جس کی تم لوگوں نے شادی کرائی یعنی مہر بیٹے پر ہے۔
[1801] (76) And if a woman marries for a thousand dirhams on the condition that he does not take her out of the city or that he does not marry another woman over her, then if he fulfills the condition, she has the specified mahr. [1802] (77) And if he marries another over her or takes her out of the city, then she has mahr al-mithl. [1801] (76) If a woman married for a thousand on condition that he will not take her out of the city or that he will not marry another woman, then if he fulfills the condition, she gets the specified mahr. The woman married for a thousand dirhams as mahr on condition that he does not take her out of the city or that he does not marry another woman after her. If he fulfills the condition, then the specified mahr is due, meaning she gets one thousand dirhams, because the husband fulfilled the condition: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' [1802] (77) And if he marries another over her or takes her out of the city, then she has mahr al-mithl. The condition was that he would not marry another or take her out. But the husband did not fulfill these conditions; rather he married another or took her out, so now she does not get the specified mahr but mahr al-mithl. She agreed to one thousand with the condition fulfilled; if he does not fulfill, she would not agree to one thousand. Therefore the standard is mahr al-mithl, as if no mahr was specified.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents two connected rulings (mas'ala) from the Hanafi school regarding marriage contracts with conditions. The matn states: If a woman marries on the condition that her husband does not take her out of her city or does not marry a second wife, and she specifies a mahr (e.g., 1000 dirhams), then if he fulfills the condition, she receives that specified mahr. If he breaches the condition by either marrying another wife or taking her out of the city, then she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). The commentator explains the rationale: the woman consented to the specified mahr only with the condition; if the condition is broken, her consent is invalidated, and the mahr reverts to the default of mahr al-mithl, as if no mahr was specified. The commentator also cites the principle 'al-muslimoon 'ala shurootihim' (Muslims are bound by their conditions). This illustrates that conditions in a marriage contract that are valid (i.e., not contrary to shariah) are enforceable, and their breach can affect the mahr obligation.

Key Terms
المسمى (al-musamma): The specified mahr (the amount agreed upon in the contract)
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to what women of similar status receive

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The specified mahr (musamma)
B) Half the specified mahr
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) No mahr

Key Takeaway
A valid condition in a marriage contract can change the mahr obligation: fulfillment gives the specified mahr, breach gives mahr al-mithl.

Mahr Specified as an Unspecified Animal: The Middle Grade
Ruling on mahr when type is specified but quality is not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when mahr is specified as an animal without description, and apply the rule of the middle grade (al-wasat) to determine the mahr amount.

Core Idea
If the mahr species is specified but not its quality, the woman receives the middle grade — avoiding harm to either party.

In a marriage contract, the mahr may be specified as an animal (e.g., a horse) without describing its quality. Is such a specification valid? What does the woman receive? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the specification is valid and the woman is entitled to the middle grade (al-wasat), with the husband having an option to give the animal or its value. We also explore the proofs from hadith and Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine that the mahr is specified only by type (e.g., horse) and not by quality (high/low). Note that the species is known but the grade is not.
This is different from specifying 'animal' without species, which is jahl kamil.
2
State the legal ruling
The specification is valid (sahih). The woman is entitled to the middle grade (al-wasat) of that animal. The husband may fulfill by giving the middle grade animal or its value.
The middle grade is determined by market value, not arbitrary selection.
3
Analyze the proofs
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'her mahr like the mahr of her peers, neither deficient nor excessive' (la waks wa la shatat). Also the Quranic principle of 'bil-ma'ruf' (what is reasonable). Both support the average grade.
The proofs are ahad hadith and Quranic general principle, establishing the rule by example.
4
Distinguish complete ignorance
If even the type is unspecified (e.g., 'animal' without horse/cow), there is jahl kamil → the mahr specification is invalid, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.
This edge case clarifies the boundaries of the rule.

The husband has the choice: if he wants, he gives the middle grade animal, and if he wants, he gives its value. However, the average is determined by value, so the husband also has the right to buy and give the average animal or give its value, because the average is known by value. If even the species is not specified (e.g., 'animal' without specifying horse or cow), then there is complete ignorance, so mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of mahr when a marriage contract specifies a type of animal (e.g., a horse) without describing its quality. The ruling is that such specification is valid, and the woman is entitled to the middle grade of that animal ('al-wast'). The husband has an option: either to give that average animal or to give its monetary value. The commentator supports this with a hadith from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who in a case where a woman's mahr was not specified and her husband died, ruled that she should get the average mahr of her peers, 'neither deficient nor excessive.' He also cites a Quranic verse about providing for divorced women 'according to what is reasonable' (bil-ma'ruf), which supports the principle of the average. If the species is not specified (e.g., just 'animal'), there is complete uncertainty (jahl kamil), which invalidates the specification, and mahr al-mithl becomes due. The key distinction is between specifying the type without description (valid, middle grade) and not specifying even the type (invalid, mahr al-mithl).

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): The middle grade of the specified animal, neither high nor low quality
غير موصوف (ghayr mawsuf): Not described in terms of quality; only the type is specified
جھالت کاملہ (jahl kamil): Complete ignorance: when even the type of the mahr item is unspecified

Key Takeaway
When a mahr is specified with the type of animal but no quality, the woman is entitled to the middle grade (al-wasat), and the husband may give the animal or its value.

Mahr Specified as an Undescribed Garment: Complete Ignorance Triggers Mahr al-Mithl
Ruling on unspecified garment mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when mahr is specified as a garment without description and explain why jahl kamil invalidates the specification, leading to mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
An undescribed garment as mahr is invalid due to complete ignorance; she gets mahr al-mithl.

In a marriage contract, the mahr must be specified with sufficient clarity. If the mahr is said to be 'a garment' but no description is given, the specification is defective because garments vary enormously in type, fabric, and value. The Hanafi school rules that such complete ignorance (jahl kamil) renders the specification void, and the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl — the mahr of women of her status. This lesson explains the ruling and its basis in the principle that complete ignorance in an essential term invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is a marriage contract where the mahr is a garment without any description. The ruling from the text: 'فلهاثوب non موصوف فلها مهر مثلها' — she receives mahr al-mithl. Determine the hukm level: wajib (obligatory).
The ruling is clear and does not require additional proof in this passage.
2
Define 'jahl kamil' (Complete Ignorance)
Jahl kamil refers to fundamental uncertainty that makes the mahr effectively unspecified. Here, because garments have many types, not describing them leaves the object of the mahr unknown, rendering the specification null.
Contrast with jahl yasir (partial ignorance) which does not invalidate.
3
Distinguish from Valid Specification
The commentary notes that if the mahr were an animal like a horse, specifying the type without description is valid because a middle grade can be determined. For garments, the variety is too vast, so description is required. Understand the reasoning.
This distinction is based on the degree of variation in the class of objects.
4
Apply the General Principle
The underlying principle: when there is jahl kamil in the mahr specification, it is as if no mahr was specified, so mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. Generalize: any mahr term that is completely unknown defaults to mahr al-mithl.
This principle applies to all mahr specifications, not only garments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۰۴] (۷۹) ولو تزوجها على ثوب غير موصوف فلها مهر مثلها [۱۸۰۴] (۷۹) اور اگر شادی کی ایسے کپڑے پر جس کی صفت بیان نہ کی گئی ہو تو عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہو گا۔ کپڑا بہت قسم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر صفت بیان نہیں کی تو مہر مجھول رہ گیا تو گویا کہ مہر متعین نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے اس عورت کے لئے مہرمشل ہوگا۔ صول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ جہالت کا ملہ ہو تو گویا کہ مہر متعین نہیں ہوا اس لئے مہر مثل لازم ہو گا۔
[1804] (79) And if he marries her on a garment that is not described, then she has mahr al-mithl. [1804] (79) And if he marries on a garment whose description is not given, then she gets mahr al-mithl. Garments are of many types. If no description is given, the mahr remains unknown (majhul), so as if no mahr was specified. Therefore she gets mahr al-mithl. The principle is: when there is complete ignorance (jahl kamil), it is as if no mahr was specified, thus mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between specifying a type (like an animal) without description, which is valid, and specifying a garment without description, which is not valid, because garments vary widely in type, fabric, and value. The text states that if the mahr is a garment without any description, the specification fails due to complete ignorance (jahl kamil), and the woman receives mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). The commentator explains that since garments come in many varieties, not describing them leaves the mahr unknown (majhul), rendering the specification null. This follows the principle that complete ignorance in the mahr invalidates the specification and defaults to mahr al-mithl. This contrasts with the previous ruling on animals, where specifying the type (e.g., horse) without description is valid because the middle grade can be determined, but for garments, the variety is too great to determine a middle without description.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): Mahr equivalent to what women of similar status receive; default when mahr is unspecified or invalid
جھالت کاملہ (jahl kamil): Complete ignorance or uncertainty that renders a specification invalid

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The most expensive garment
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) No mahr, because the contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
Complete ignorance (jahl kamil) in mahr specification invalidates it, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

Invalidity of Mut'ah and Temporary Marriage
Ruling that mut'ah and time-limited marriage are invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah and temporary marriage and identify why they are batil.

Core Idea
Any marriage with a time limit is void — mut'ah and muwaqqat are both batil.

This lesson covers a clear and decisive ruling from the Hanafi school: any marriage contract that includes a specified duration is invalid from the start. The text states that both nikah al-mut'ah (pleasure marriage) and nikah al-muwaqqat (time-limited marriage) are batil. This is a fundamental position, based on the consensus of the Companions and the abrogation of earlier permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited marriage forms
Find the Arabic terms نكاح المتعة and نكاح الموقت in the text. These refer to temporary marriage contracts.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its implication
The text says both are 'باطل' (invalid). This means the contract is void ab initio, with no legal effects—no mahr, no inheritance, no divorce needed.
This is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

[1805] (80) And mut'ah marriage and time-limited marriage are invalid. [1805] (80) Mut'ah marriage and time-limited marriage are invalid.

Commentary
This is a short, decisive ruling from the Hanafi school. The text states that nikah al-mut'ah (pleasure marriage, where a man marries a woman for a specified period in exchange for payment) and nikah al-muwaqqat (marriage with a fixed term) are both batil (invalid). This is a fundamental position of the Hanafi school, based on the consensus of the Companions and abrogation of the permissibility of mut'ah. The ruling is clear and categorical: any marriage that is conditioned on a time limit is void. The commentary repeats the same rule in Urdu.

Key Terms

نكاح موقت (nikah al-muwaqqat): A marriage with a specified time limit, also invalid

Marriage with Unspecified Animal as Mahr: Validity and Amount
Ruling on validity and amount of mahr when animal is specified without description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when an animal is specified without description, identify the wife's entitlement to the average, and apply the husband's option to give the animal or its value.

Core Idea
When mahr is specified as an animal without description, the wife gets the average; the husband may give the animal or its value.

This passage addresses a common scenario in marriage contracts where the mahr is specified as an animal (e.g., a horse) but without describing its quality. The Hanafi school rules that such a specification is valid (صحت التسمية), and the wife is entitled to the average quality of that animal. The husband also has the option to give the monetary value instead. This ruling is supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (رضي الله عنه) and the Quranic principle of fairness (المعروف). The passage also distinguishes between partial ambiguity (species specified) and total ambiguity (species unspecified), which leads to mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is specifying an animal as mahr without describing its quality. The ruling is that the specification is valid (sahih) and the marriage is valid.
This ruling applies when the animal's species (jins) is mentioned but not its quality (sifah).
2
Determine the wife's entitlement
The wife is entitled to the average (wasat) of that animal – neither the best nor the worst, but the middle in value.
The average is determined by market value of similar animals in that locality.
3
Identify the husband's options
The husband has two choices: give the animal itself (at average quality) or give its monetary value.
This option prevents hardship; the husband can give cash if the animal is unavailable.
4
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'لها مهر مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط' (She gets the dower of her peers, neither less nor more). Also Quran 2:241: provision with what is reasonable (المعروف).
The hadith establishes the principle of average without excess or deficiency.
5
Distinguish total ambiguity
If the animal's species is also unspecified (e.g., just 'animal'), then there is complete ignorance (جهالة كاملة) and the mahr becomes mahr al-mithl (dower of peers).
Partial ambiguity is tolerated; total ambiguity invalidates the specification.

اگر جانور کی جنس بھی متعین نہیں کی۔ مثلا یوں نہیں کہا کہ گھوڑا مہر ہے یا گائے بلکہ یوں کہا کہ جانور پر نکاح کرتا ہوں تو اس میں جہالت کاملہ ہے اس لئے مہر مثل لازم ہوگا۔
And if he marries her upon an animal not described, the specification is valid, and she gets the middle (average) of it, and the husband has the choice: if he wishes, he gives her that, and if he wishes, he gives her its value.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding mahr (dower) when it is specified as an animal but without describing its quality or species in detail. The ruling states that the specification is valid (صحّت التسمية). The wife is entitled to the average (الوسط) of that animal, meaning neither the best nor the worst. The husband has the option to give either the animal itself (at the average level) or its monetary value. The commentary elaborates with an example: if the husband says 'I marry you on a horse' without specifying high or low quality, the mahr is valid, and the wife gets a horse of average quality and price. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (رضي الله عنه) who ruled for a woman whose husband died without fixing a mahr that she should get the mahr al-mithl (like her peers' dower) 'neither less nor more' (لا وكس ولا شطط). The Quranic verse (البقرة:241) about providing for divorced women 'according to what is reasonable' (بالمعروف) also supports this principle of what is customary and fair. The commentary further notes that if the species of the animal is also unspecified (e.g., just 'animal' without saying horse or cow), then the ignorance is complete (جہالت کاملہ) and mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers) becomes obligatory, not the specified animal. This distinguishes between partial and total ambiguity (جهالة).

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Dower or bridal gift, obligatory from husband to wife in marriage.
وسط (wasat): The average or middle quality, neither best nor worst, in terms of value.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The specification of mahr at the time of marriage contract.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or ambiguity regarding the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman specifying an animal as mahr (e.g., a horse) without describing its quality, what is the ruling?
A) The mahr is invalid and the woman gets no mahr.
B) The mahr is valid and the woman gets the best of that animal.
C) The mahr is valid and the woman gets the average of that animal; the husband may give the animal or its value.
D) The mahr is invalid and the woman gets mahr al-mithl.

Key Takeaway
When an animal is specified as mahr without description, the mahr is valid, the wife gets the average, and the husband may give the animal or its value.

Marriage with Unspecified Cloth as Mahr
Ruling on mahr when cloth is unspecified - mahr al-mithl due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when mahr is specified as an unspecified cloth and explain why mahr al-mithl becomes due.

Core Idea
Complete ignorance (jahalah kamilah) invalidates mahr specification, triggering mahr al-mithl.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario from the matn of Al-Quduri where a man marries a woman on a cloth as mahr but without any description. The text rules that the mahr specification is invalid due to complete ignorance (jahalah), and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl. The commentary explains why an unspecified cloth is different from an unspecified animal. This lesson will help you identify the boundary between valid and invalid mahr specifications in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the issue
The act is a marriage contract where the mahr is specified as 'a cloth' but without any description (type, quality, etc.). The issue is whether this specification is valid.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The marriage is sahih (valid), but the mahr specification is invalid. Consequently, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers).
The contract is not void because the mahr is not a pillar (rukn) of marriage; it is an obligation (wajib).
3
Analyze the cause (illah)
The specification is invalid due to jahalah kamilah (complete ignorance) about the mahr object. A cloth has many varieties, and without description, the mahr remains entirely unknown, which the law does not tolerate.
Partial ignorance (jahalah qalilah) may be tolerated if the object is still identifiable.
4
Compare with similar cases
Contrast this with an unspecified animal (e.g., a camel without description). There, the species is known, so ignorance is partial and the specification is valid. The difference lies in the degree of ignorance.
The key is whether the specification removes complete ignorance.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If a man marries a woman specifying 'a cloth' without describing it, the woman receives mahr al-mithl. The court will determine her mahr based on her peers (family, age, beauty, etc.).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تزوجها على ثوب غير موصوف فلها مهر مثلها
اور اگر شادی کی ایسے کپڑے پر جس کی صفت بیان نہ کی گئی ہو تو عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہو گا۔ کپڑا بہت قسم کا ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر صفت بیان نہیں کی تو مہر مجھول رہ گیا تو گویا کہ مہر متعین نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے اس عورت کے لئے مهر مثل ہوگا۔
And if he marries her upon a cloth not described, then she has the mahr of her peers (mahr al-mithl).
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when the mahr is specified as a cloth but without any description of its type, quality, or value. Unlike the previous case of an animal (where the species was known even if not described), a cloth has many varieties (e.g., silk, cotton, different weaves), and without any description, the mahr remains unknown (مجهول). Therefore, the specification (تسمية) is invalid, and the wife becomes entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers). The commentary explains the underlying principle: complete ignorance (جهالة كاملة) about the mahr object makes the specification ineffective, leading to mahr al-mithl as the default obligation. This is qiyas on the case where no mahr is specified at all.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of her social standing (family, beauty, age, etc.) receive.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or ambiguity regarding the mahr object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman specifying 'a cloth' as mahr without any description, what is the ruling?
A) The mahr specification is valid, and she gets an average cloth.
B) The mahr specification is invalid, and she gets mahr al-mithl.
C) The mahr specification is invalid, and the marriage is void.
D) She gets the best cloth available in the market.

Key Takeaway
When mahr is specified with complete ignorance (jahalah kamilah) about the object, the specification fails and mahr al-mithl becomes due.

Mut'ah and Temporary Marriage are Invalid
Ruling that mut'ah and temporary marriage are invalid (batil)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah and temporary marriage and explain the primary proofs from Quran and Sunnah that establish their invalidity.

Core Idea
Mut'ah and temporary marriage are invalid (batil) and haram; permanent prohibition established by Quran and Hadith.

This lesson addresses two types of marriage contracts that are explicitly prohibited in the Hanafi school: nikah al-mut'ah (pleasure marriage) and nikah al-muwaqqat (temporary marriage). Both were initially permitted in early Islam but were permanently forbidden by the Prophet (ﷺ) at the Conquest of Makkah. The passage provides the Quranic verse and hadith that serve as the definitive proof for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states that both mut'ah and temporary marriage are 'batil' (invalid). Determine what these terms mean and the legal consequence.
Mut'ah: a marriage for a fixed term in exchange for payment. Temporary marriage: a marriage with a specified duration with witnesses.
2
Locate the primary dalil (Quran)
The passage cites Quran 23:6 which restricts lawful sexual relations to wives and slave-girls. Understand how this verse is applied to mut'ah.
The verse uses 'azwaj' (wives) and 'ma malakat aymanuhum' (slave-girls). In mut'ah, the woman is not a permanent wife, so relations fall outside these categories.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of the Quranic proof
The legal implication (wajh al-dalalah) is that any sexual relationship beyond wife or slave-girl is transgression ('ādūn). Since mut'ah and temporary marriage do not create a full wife, they are included in this prohibition.
The Hanafi school holds that the verse's generality ('amm) includes all non-wife/non-slave relations, making mut'ah haram.
4
Analyze the Sunnah proof
The hadith from al-Rabī' ibn Sabrah al-Juhanī reports the Prophet's statement that the previous permission for mut'ah is now forbidden until Judgment Day. This hadith abrogates (naskh) the earlier permissibility.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and other collections; its authenticity is accepted by all Sunni schools.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
While all Sunni schools agree on prohibition, the Shia Ithna-ashari school permits mut'ah. Understand that the Hanafi position is based on the definitive texts and their interpretation.
The difference arises from the Shia view that the prohibition was not permanent or that the relevant hadith are not accepted by them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونكاح المتعة والموقت باطل
نکاح متعہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت سے کہے کہ میں تم سے کچھ رقم دے کر کچھ دنوں کے لئے فائدہ اٹھانا چاہتا ہوں ۔ یہ نکاح پہلے جائز تھا۔ فتح مکہ کے موقع پر قیامت تک کے لئے حرام کر دیا گیا اور اب بالکل جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نکاح موقت کی شکل یہ ہے کہ دو گواہوں کی گواہی سے متعین دن کے لئے نکاح کرے۔ یہ دونوں نکاح باطل ہیں۔ آیت میں ہے۔ الا علی ازواجهم او ما ملكت ايمانهم فانهم غير ملومين فمن ابتغى وراء ذلک فاولئک هم العادون (الف) (آیت ۶ سورۃ المؤمنون (۲۳) اس آیت میں ہے کہ صرف بیوی سے صحبت کرے یا باندی سے صحبت کرے۔ اس کے علاوہ سے زیادتی ہے۔ اور نکاح متعہ میں اور نکاح موقت میں عورت بیوی نہیں ہوتی اس لئے ان سے صحبت کرنا ظلم ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ حدثني الربيع بن سبرة الجهني ان اباه حدثه انه كان مع رسول الله الله الله فقال يا ايها الناس اني قد كنت اذنت لكم في الاستمتاع من النساء وان الله قد حرم ذلك الى يوم القيامة فمن كان عنده منهن شيء فليخل سبيله ولا تأخذوا مما آتيتموهن شيئا (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب نکاح المحمد و بیان اند ایج ثم نسخ ثم ان ثم نسخ واستقر تحریمہ الی یوم القیامة ص ۴۵۰ نمبر ۱۴۰۶ر بخاری شریف ، باب بھی النبی من الان عن نکاح المحعه اخیر اص ۷۶۶ نمبر ۵۱۱۵ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فانکاح المحة ص ۲۹۰ نمبر ۲۰۷۳ ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تحریم نکاح المحعه ص ۲۱۳ نمبر (۱۱۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نکاح متعہ منسوخ ہے اور حرام ہے۔ اور نکاح موقت بھی اسی میں داخل ہے۔
And mut'ah marriage and temporary marriage are invalid.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage declares the ruling that both nikah mut'ah (marriage for pleasure, often for a fixed term) and nikah muwaqqat (temporary marriage with a fixed duration) are invalid (باطل) in the Hanafi school. The commentary explains the nature of mut'ah: a man says 'I wish to enjoy you for some days in exchange for some money'. This was permitted initially in early Islam but was permanently prohibited (حرام) on the occasion of the Conquest of Makkah, and the prohibition remains until the Day of Judgment. Temporary marriage is defined as a marriage contracted for a specified number of days with witnesses. Both are batil. The proof is from the Quran (المؤمنون:6) which limits lawful sexual relations to wives (زوج) and slave-girls (ما ملكت أيمانهم). In mut'ah and temporary marriage, the woman is not a wife, so such relations are transgression (عادون). The hadith narrated by al-Rabi' ibn Sabrah al-Juhani quotes the Prophet (ﷺ) saying: 'O people, I had permitted you to enjoy women (isti'mta'), but Allah has forbidden that until the Day of Judgment. So whoever has any of them with him, let him let her go, and do not take anything of what you have given them.' This hadith from Sahih Muslim and others abrogates the earlier permission. The commentary concludes that temporary marriage is included in the prohibition of mut'ah.

Key Terms
نکاح متعہ (nikah al-mut'ah): A temporary marriage contract for a fixed period or for pleasure, involving payment.
نکاح موقت (nikah al-muwaqqat): A marriage contracted for a specified duration, with witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on nikah al-mut'ah?
A) Permissible if the duration is more than one year.
B) Makruh tanzihi.
C) Haram and batil.
D) Permissible with the wife's consent.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah and temporary marriage are invalid (batil) in the Hanafi school, prohibited by Quran and Sunnah, and any sexual relations under such a contract are unlawful.

Marriage of Slave Without Master's Permission: Suspended, Not Void
Ruling on marriage of slave without master's permission: suspended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a slave's marriage without master's permission is suspended (mawquf) and explain the interpretation of the hadith that supports this.

Core Idea
A slave's marriage without permission is suspended, not void—it awaits the master's approval.

In the pre-modern legal system, slaves had capacity to contract marriage, but their authority was limited by the master's guardianship. This passage addresses the scenario where a slave contracts marriage without that permission. The Hanafi school takes a nuanced position: the marriage is not automatically invalid but suspended. This balances the slave's capacity with the master's authority, as we will see from the proof and the school's interpretive approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Marriage by a slave without master's permission. What is the ruling? It is suspended (mawquf).
Mawquf means the contract's validity is contingent on a future condition.
2
Understand the meaning of mawquf
A suspended contract is neither valid nor invalid immediately; its fate hinges on a condition (here, permission).
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (ﷺ) said such a marriage is 'batil'. How does the Hanafi school reconcile this with their ruling of suspension?
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The word 'batil' is interpreted in light of the slave's legal capacity and the principle of istihsan, leading to suspension rather than outright voidness.
The Hanafis interpret 'batil' as 'not effective without permission'.
5
Note the practical outcome
If permission is granted, the marriage becomes valid from inception; if rejected, it is nullified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتزويج العبد والامة بغير اذن مولاهما موقوف فان اجازه المولى جاز وان رده بطل
غلام اور باندی کا نکاح بغیر آقا کی اجازت کے موقوف ہے۔ پس اگر آقا اس کی اجازت دے تو جائز ہوگا اور اگر رد کر دے تو باطل ہوگا ان غلام یا باندی نے بغیر مولی کی اجازت کے شادی کر لی تو یہ نکاح اس کی اجازت پر موقوف رہے گا ۔ اگر مولی نے اجازت دی تو جائز ہو جائے گا اور رد کر دیا تو نکاح باطل ہو جائے۔ حدیث گزرچکی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر عن النبی الله الله قال اذا نكح العبد بغير اذن مولاه فنكاحه باطل (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی نکاح العبد بغیر اذن موالیہ ص ۲۹۱ نمبر ۲۰۷۹ ترمذی شریف، نمبر ۱۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام باندی کا نکاح بغیر آقا کی اجازت کے باطل ہے۔
And the marriage of a male slave and a female slave without the permission of their master is suspended; if the master permits it, it becomes valid, and if he rejects it, it becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of slaves (both male and female) without the permission of their owner. The marriage is not automatically valid or invalid; it is suspended (مَوْقُوف) upon the master's permission. If the master subsequently grants permission, the marriage becomes valid (جائز) from the time of contract. If the master rejects it, the marriage becomes invalid (باطل). The commentary explains that if a slave or female slave marries without the master's permission, the marriage remains in a state of suspension until the master's decision. The supporting hadith from Ibn 'Umar (رضي الله عنه) reports the Prophet (ﷺ) saying: 'If a slave marries without his master's permission, his marriage is invalid.' However, the Hanafi school interprets 'invalid' (باطل) in the hadith as meaning that the marriage is not effective until the master's permission; thus it is suspended, not automatically void. This is an example of istihsan balancing the hadith with other considerations.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; the marriage contract's validity is contingent on subsequent permission.
مولی (mawla): Master or owner of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the status of a marriage contracted by a slave without the master's permission?
A) Immediately void (batil).
B) Valid but the master can divorce them.
C) Suspended (mawquf) on the master's permission.
D) Valid if the slave is male, but not if female.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that a slave's marriage without master's permission is suspended (mawquf) balances the slave's capacity with the master's authority, allowing the marriage to be validated by subsequent permission.

Marriage by Unauthorized Person without Consent
Ruling on marriage by fudhuli without consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a marriage contracted by a fudhuli without consent and identify the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A marriage without consent by a fudhuli is suspended — it becomes valid only if the spouses later approve.

This lesson examines the case where a third party, not a guardian, contracts a marriage for an adult man or woman without their permission. The Hanafi school treats such a marriage as suspended (mawquf), contingent upon the subsequent consent of the spouses. Understanding this ruling clarifies the fundamental role of consent in Islamic marriage and distinguishes it from cases involving guardians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the agent
Recognize that the act is a marriage contract performed by a fudhuli (unauthorized person) for an adult man or woman.
The fudhuli is neither a guardian nor has prior permission.
2
State the default ruling
The marriage is suspended (mawquf) — it is not immediately valid nor invalid.
Suspension means the contract is neither void nor fully effective until a condition is met.
3
Identify the condition for validity
The marriage becomes valid only if the spouse (or both spouses) explicitly consent after the contract.
Consent must be given freely; silence may not suffice in all cases.
4
Determine the consequence of rejection
If the spouse rejects the marriage after the fact, the contract becomes invalid (batil).
Rejection may be explicit or through clear actions.
5
Distinguish from guardian's marriage
Contrast this with a marriage by a guardian (wali) who has authority. Guardians can contract without prior consent in some cases (jabr), but a fudhuli has no such authority.
The key difference is the status of the person performing the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کذلک ان زوج رجل امرأة بغير رضاها او رجلا بغير رضاه
إیسی ہی اگر شادی کرادی کسی فضولی نے عورت کی بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے یا مرد کی بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے تو نکاح موقوف رہیگا کسی آدمی نے بالغ عورت یا بالغ مرد کی شادی بغیر ان کی رضامندی اور اجازت کے کرادی تو یہ نکاح عورت اور مرد کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے۔
And similarly, if a man marries a woman without her consent, or a man without his consent...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling of suspension to another case: when a third party (فُضُولِی - an unauthorized person) contracts a marriage for an adult woman or man without their consent. The commentary explains: if someone (not a guardian) performs the marriage of a mature woman or a mature man without their permission, the marriage is suspended (موقوف) and becomes valid only if the contracting parties later give their consent. If they reject it, the marriage becomes invalid. This is analogous to the previous case of the slave, based on the principle that the consent of the spouses is a fundamental condition for the validity of marriage (رضا is essential). The Hanafi school requires the consent of the bride and groom for the marriage to be binding; a forced marriage is not valid without their subsequent approval.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudhuli): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without their permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The marriage is immediately valid.
B) The marriage is invalid (batil) unconditionally.
C) The marriage is suspended (mawquf) on the woman's consent.
D) The marriage is valid only if the guardian consents.

Key Takeaway
A marriage contracted by an unauthorized person without the spouses' consent is suspended and only becomes valid upon their explicit ratification.

The Fuduli Marriage: Suspended Until Consent
Ruling statement explaining the suspension of a fuduli marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a fuduli marriage and explain its suspended status pending consent.

Core Idea
A marriage contracted by a fuduli is not void but suspended, awaiting the consent of the parties.

In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage contract may sometimes be arranged by a person who has no authority—neither guardianship nor agency—over the bride or groom. Such a person is called a fuduli. This passage clarifies that a marriage arranged by a fuduli without the consent of the mature parties is not immediately void; rather, it remains in a state of suspension. Only when the man and woman give their permission does the marriage become valid. If they reject it, the marriage is void. This ruling upholds the principle that the right to marry belongs to the individuals themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the fuduli
In any marriage contract, recognize who the contracting parties are: the groom, the bride, and the person acting as the contracting agent. Here, the 'fuduli' is a third party who has no legal authority (wilayah) to contract marriage on behalf of the bride or groom.
A fuduli is neither a guardian (wali) nor an appointed agent (wakil).
2
Understand the condition of consent
For a marriage to be valid, the free consent of the mature bride and groom is essential. If the fuduli contracts the marriage without their permission, the contract is defective in that condition.
Consent is a shart (condition) for the validity of the marriage.
3
Define the suspended status (mauquf)
The contract is not void (batil) nor voidable (fasid); it is 'mauquf'—suspended. Its legal effect is delayed until the parties who have the right to consent (the bride and groom) either ratify or reject it.
Suspension is a unique Hanafi concept for contracts concluded by a fuduli.
4
Determine the outcome based on ratification
If the parties give their permission (express or implied), the marriage becomes valid from the time of the contract. If they reject it, the marriage is void—as if it never occurred.
The ruling is derived from the hadith that the authority to marry rests with the individuals themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۰۷ (۸۲) ایسے ہی اگر شادی کرادی کسی فضولی نے عورت کی بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے یا مرد کی بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے تو نکاح موقوف رہیگا کسی آدمی نے بالغ عورت یا بالغ مرد کی شادی بغیر ان کی رضامندی اور اجازت کے کرادی تو یہ نکاح عورت اور مرد کی اجازت پر موقوف رہیں گے۔ اگر انہوں نے اجازت دی تو نکاح بحال رہے گا اور رد کر دیا تو رد ہو جائے گا۔ او پر حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ شادی کرنے کا اختیار خود مرد اور عورت کو ہے۔ اس لئے کسی نے ان کی اجازت کے بغیر شادی کرادی تو یہ نکاح ان کی اجازت پر موقوف رہے گا۔
[1807 (82)] Similarly, if a fuduli (unauthorized person) arranges the marriage of a woman without her consent, or of a man without his consent, then the marriage remains suspended. If a person arranges the marriage of a mature woman or a mature man without their consent and permission, then this marriage remains suspended upon the permission of the woman and man. If they permit, the marriage stands; if they reject, it is rejected. A hadith has passed that the authority to marry belongs to the man and woman themselves. Therefore, if someone arranges marriage without their permission, this marriage remains suspended upon their permission.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It extends the principle of suspended (mauquf) marriage to cases where a third party (fuduli) contracts marriage for a mature man or woman without their consent. The marriage is not automatically void; rather, it becomes valid only if the individuals themselves later give their consent. If they reject, it becomes void. The rationale given is that the right to marry belongs to the individuals themselves, as established in a previous hadith.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized person who does not have guardianship or agency to contract marriage on behalf of another.
موقوف (mauquf): Suspended; a contract that is neither valid nor void but awaiting ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of a marriage contracted by a fuduli for a mature woman without her consent?
A) The marriage is void immediately.
B) The marriage is valid if the woman does not object.
C) The marriage is suspended until the woman permits.
D) The marriage is only valid if the fuduli is a relative.

Key Takeaway
A fuduli marriage is not automatically void; it is suspended and becomes valid only upon the consent of the mature parties.

Can a Paternal Cousin Marry His Cousin as Her Guardian?
Ruling with proof: permissibility of paternal cousin marrying his cousin as her guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a paternal cousin acting as both guardian and groom, and cite the proof from the Prophet's actions.

Core Idea
It is permissible for a paternal cousin to marry his cousin by acting as her guardian, based on the Prophet's own practice.

Marriage requires a guardian (wali) for the woman. But what happens when the prospective groom himself is the closest male relative? The Hanafi school addresses this with clarity, drawing directly from the Prophet's sunnah. In this lesson, we explore the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Read the passage to understand the specific scenario: a paternal cousin (ibn al-am) marrying his paternal cousin (bint al-am) by acting as her guardian. The ruling is stated as ja'iz (permissible).
2
Understand the guardian hierarchy
The text lists closer relatives (son, father, grandfather, brother, paternal uncle) who take precedence. In their absence, the paternal cousin becomes the asabah and thus the wali.
The order of asabah is critical in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the dual role (asil and wakil)
The cousin acts as asil (principal/groom) from his own side and as wakil (agent) from the woman's side. The text explains that one person can represent both sides or act as wakil for one side and asil for the other.
The formula 'Zawwajtu' in front of two witnesses executes the contract.
4
Examine the proofs
Two hadith are cited: the Prophet marrying Aisha (he was asil and wakil) and the hadith of Sahl bin Sa'd (Prophet as wakil for both). These establish the precedent.
The proofs are from Sahih Bukhari, hadith of ahad status but accepted in practice.
5
Conclude applicability
Since the Prophet's actions validate the dual role, the cousin can marry his cousin directly, provided no closer guardian exists and two witnesses are present.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۸۰۸ (۸۳) جائز ہے چچا زاد بھائی کے لئے شادی کرے چازاد بہن سے خود سے۔ بیٹا، باپ، دادا، بھائی اور چانہ ہوں تو اب چچا زاد بھائی لڑکی کا عصبہ اور ولی بنتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ لڑکی کا ولی بنا اور اپنی جانب سے اصیل ہوا۔ اور نکاح میں ایک ہی آدمی دونوں طرف سے ولی بن سکتا ہے۔ یا ایک طرف سے وکیل اور اپنی جانب سے اصیل بن سکتا ہے۔ اور دو گواہوں کے سامنے نکحت کہا تو دونوں جانب سے ایجاب و قبول ادا ہو گئے اور نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ اپنی جانب سے اصیل ہو اور لڑکی کی مجانب سے وکیل ہو اور نکحت کہنے سے نکاح ہو جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة ان النبی تزوجها وهي بنت ست سنين (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب تزویج الاب ابنته من الامام ص اے سے نمبر ۵۱۳۴) اس حدیث میں حضور اپنی جانب سے اصیل تھے اور حضرت عائشہ کی جانب سے وکیل تھے اور ان سے آپ نے شادی کی۔ اور دونوں جانب سے وکیل ہو اور شادی کرا دے اس کی دلیل لمبی حدیث کا یہ لکڑا ہے۔ حدثنا سهل بن سعد ... قال ا ا ل ل له اذهب فقد زوجتكها بما معك من القرآن (ب) ( بخاری شریف باب اذا کان الونی ھو الخاطب ص ۷۷۰ نمبر ۵۱۳۲) اس حدیث میں حضور بیوی اور شوہر دونوں جانب سے وکیل تھے۔ اور ایک ہی لفظ زوجتکھا سے دونوں کی شادی کرادی۔ اس لئے چچازاد بھائی خود چچازاد بہن سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ چازاد بھائی کے لئے چچازاد بہن سے شادی کرنا جائز ہے۔
1808 (83) It is permissible for a paternal cousin to marry his paternal cousin himself. When there are son, father, grandfather, brother, and paternal uncle, then the paternal cousin becomes the asabah and guardian of the girl. So he becomes the guardian for the girl and becomes the principal (asil) from his own side. In marriage, one person can be guardian from both sides, or he can be agent (wakil) from one side and principal from the other. When he says 'Zawwajtu' (I marry) in front of two witnesses, the offer and acceptance are executed from both sides, and the marriage takes place. He is principal from his side and wakil from the girl's side, and by saying 'Zawwajtu' the marriage occurs. The proof is the hadith from Aisha that the Prophet married her when she was six years old (Bukhari). In this hadith, the Prophet was principal from his side and wakil from Aisha's side. Another proof is the long hadith of Sahl bin Sa'd: the Prophet said to a man: 'Go, I have married her to you with what you have of the Quran.' In this hadith, the Prophet was agent from both sides. So a paternal cousin can marry his paternal cousin himself, because it is permissible for a paternal cousin to marry his paternal cousin.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It explains that a paternal cousin (ibn al-am) can marry his paternal cousin (bint al-am) by acting as her guardian (wali) from her side and as the groom from his own side. The text provides the sequence of guardians: the girl's son, father, grandfather, brother, and paternal uncle take precedence; in their absence, the paternal cousin becomes her asabah (agnate heir) and thus her guardian. He can then contract marriage by saying 'Zawwajtu' (I marry) in front of two witnesses, acting for both parties. The proofs are from the sunnah: the Prophet (saw) married Aisha acting as principal for himself and wakil for her, and in the hadith of Sahl bin Sa'd, he acted as wakil for both parties. Hence, this is valid.

Key Terms
عصبه (asabah): Agnate male relative who is entitled to inheritance and can act as guardian in marriage.
اصیل (asil): Principal party to the contract; here, the groom himself.
وکیل (wakil): Agent representing another party in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse on marriage
B) The Prophet marrying Aisha
C) The practice of the Sahaba
D) The consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
A paternal cousin can validly marry his cousin by acting as her wali, based on the Prophet's own practice.

Woman Authorizing a Man to Marry Her to Himself
Ruling on woman appointing a man as wakil to marry her to himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman appointing a man as her wakil to marry her to himself and cite the prophetic precedent.

Core Idea
One may be both groom and agent in marriage; the Prophet's marriage to Aisha is proof.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in marriage contracts: can a man whom a woman appoints as her wakil also be the groom? The Hanafi school permits it, based on a clear precedent from the Prophet's own marriage. We'll examine the ruling, the evidence, and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Identify the act described: a woman authorizes a man to marry her to himself. Determine the ruling: the marriage is valid (ja'iz) according to the Hanafi school.
The text explicitly says 'jaza' (it is permissible).
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Aisha, where the Prophet married her acting as both groom and her agent. Note the source: Sahih Bukhari.
The hadith is mentioned as proof that one person can combine both roles.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's action demonstrates that it is permissible for one person to be both the principal (asil) and the agent (wakil) in a marriage contract when authorized by the woman.
The proof is direct: the Prophet is the model (uswah hasanah).
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Recognize that some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require a separate guardian (wali) for the woman, and may not permit one person to act as both. Understand the opposing position.
The Hanafi position is stronger due to the prophetic precedent.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) based on Zahir al-Riwayah. The evidence is clear and not overridden by istihsan.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah would uphold this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۰۹ (۸۴) واذا اذنت المرأة لرجل ان يزوجها من نفسه فعقد بحضرة شاهدين جاز . عورت نے ایک آدمی کو اپنی شادی کا وکیل بنایا کہ وہ اپنی شادی اس عورت سے کرے۔ پس اس آدمی نے دو گواہوں کے سامنے نکحت کہہ کر اپنا نکاح اس عورت سے کر دیا تو نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنی جانب سے امیل ہوا اور عورت کی جانب سے وکیل ہوا۔ اور نکاح میں ایک ہی آدمی وکیل اور اصیل بن سکتا ہے (۲) اوپر حدیث گزری عن عائشة ان النبي عل الله تزوجها وهى بنت ست سنين (ج) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۵۱۳۴) جس میں حضور اپنی جانب سے اصیل اور حضرت عائشہ کی جانب سے وکیل تھے (۳) نکاح میں وکیل موکل کی جانب سے سفیر اور معجر ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ دونوں
[1809 (84)] And if a woman permits a man to marry her to himself, and he contracts in the presence of two witnesses, it is permissible. A woman appointed a man as her wakil (agent) to marry her to himself. So that man said 'Zawwajtu' in front of two witnesses, marrying himself to that woman, and the marriage becomes valid. Because he became principal from his side and wakil from the woman's side. And in marriage, one person can be both wakil and asil. The hadith of Aisha has passed: the Prophet married her when she was six years old, in which the Prophet was asil from his side and wakil from Aisha's side. In marriage, the wakil acts as representative and agent for the principal, so he can act for both.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if a woman authorizes a man to marry her to himself, and he contracts the marriage with two witnesses, it is valid. The man acts as the groom (asil) from his own side and as the woman's agent (wakil) from her side. The text cites the same hadith of the Prophet marrying Aisha, where he acted as asil for himself and wakil for her, as proof. This shows that one person can combine both roles in a marriage contract.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): Agent appointed to contract marriage on behalf of the principal.
اصیل (asil): Principal party to the contract; here, the groom himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Permissibility of a Paternal Cousin Marrying His Cousin
Ruling with proof on paternal cousin marrying his cousin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a paternal cousin marrying his cousin and explain the hadith-based proof for a person acting as both guardian and groom.

Core Idea
A paternal cousin can marry his cousin because he is her 'asaba and can be both guardian and groom, as proven by the Prophet's marriage to Aisha.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in marriage guardianship: when the closest male relatives are absent, a paternal cousin becomes the 'asaba and thus the marriage guardian. The text rules that he may marry his paternal cousin directly, acting as both guardian from her side and groom from his. This ruling is supported by two hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) acted in dual capacities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of a paternal cousin marrying his paternal cousin. The text states it is permissible (yajuz), establishing the hukm as mubah.
The ruling is a matter of permissibility, not obligation.
2
Understand the legal capacity
The paternal cousin is the woman's 'asaba (residuary heir) in the absence of closer male relatives, making him her marriage guardian (wali). He acts as principal (asil) from his own side and guardian from hers.
One person can hold both capacities: wali for the woman and groom for himself.
3
Examine the first proof
The hadith of Aisha: the Prophet married her while being her guardian (acting as agent) and his own principal. This demonstrates the permissibility of one person acting in both roles.
Hadith reference: Bukhari no. 5134.
4
Examine the second proof
The hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd: the Prophet acted as agent for both the groom and the bride using a single utterance. This shows that even simultaneous dual agency is allowed.
Hadith reference: Bukhari no. 5132.
5
Conclude the ruling
Both proofs together establish that a paternal cousin can marry his cousin by being both wali and groom. The Hanafi school relies on these precedents.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۳) ويجوز لابن العم ان يزوج بنت عمه من نفسه. [جائز ہے چچا زاد بھائی کے لئے شادی کرے چچازاد بہن سے خود سے۔] بيٹا، باپ، دادا، بھائی اور چانہ ہوں تو اب چچا زاد بھائی لڑکی کا عصبہ اور ولی بنتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ لڑکی کا ولی بنا اور اپنی جانب سے اصیل ہوا۔ اور نکاح میں ایک ہی آدمی دونوں طرف سے ولی بن سکتا ہے۔ یا ایک طرف سے وکیل اور اپنی جانب سے اصیل بن سکتا ہے۔ اور دو گواہوں کے سامنے نکحت کہا تو دونوں جانب سے ایجاب و قبول ادا ہو گئے اور نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ اپنی جانب سے اصیل ہو اور لڑکی کی مجانب سے وکیل ہو اور نکحت کہنے سے نکاح ہو جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة ان النبی الله تزوجها وهي بنت ست سنين (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب تزویج الاب ابنته من الامام ص اے سے نمبر ۵۱۳۴) اس حدیث میں حضور اپنی جانب سے اصیل تھے اور حضرت عائشہ کی جانب سے وکیل تھے اور ان سے آپ نے شادی کی۔ اور دونوں جانب سے وکیل ہو اور شادی کرا دے اس کی دلیل لمبی حدیث کا یہ لکڑا ہے۔ حدثنا سهل بن سعد ... قال ا ا ل ل له اذهب فقد زوجتكها بما معك من القرآن (ب) ( بخاری شریف باب اذا کان الونی ھو الخاطب ص ۷۷۰ نمبر ۵۱۳۲) اس حدیث میں حضور بیوی اور شوہر دونوں جانب سے وکیل تھے۔ اور ایک ہی لفظ زوجتکھا سے دونوں کی شادی کرادی۔ اس لئے چچازاد بھائی خود چچازاد بہن سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ چازاد بھائی کے لئے چچازاد بہن سے شادی کرنا جائز ہے۔
(83) It is permissible for the son of the paternal uncle to marry the daughter of his paternal uncle from himself. [It is permissible for a paternal cousin to marry his paternal cousin from himself.] When there is a son, father, grandfather, brother, or paternal uncle, then the paternal cousin becomes the 'asaba and guardian of the girl. Therefore he becomes the girl's guardian and is a principal from his own side. In marriage, one man can be a guardian from both sides, or he can be an agent from one side and a principal from his own side. If he says 'I marry' in the presence of two witnesses, then the offer and acceptance are fulfilled from both sides and the marriage takes place. Being a principal from his own side and an agent from the girl's side, saying 'I marry' effects the marriage. Its proof is this hadith: from Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) married her when she was six years old (Bukhari, chapter on a father giving his daughter in marriage to the imam, no. 5134). In this hadith, the Prophet was a principal from his side and an agent from Aisha's side, and he married her. And the proof for both sides being an agent is this piece of a long hadith: We were told by Sahl ibn Sa'd ... he said: Go, I have married you to her with what you have of the Quran (Bukhari, chapter on when the guardian is the suitor, p. 770 no. 5132). In this hadith, the Prophet was an agent from both the wife's and husband's sides, and he performed the marriage with a single phrase 'Zawwajtukaha'. Therefore a paternal cousin can marry his paternal cousin, because it is permissible for a paternal cousin to marry his paternal cousin.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the permissibility of a paternal cousin (ibn 'amm) acting as both guardian and groom when marrying his paternal cousin (bint 'amm). The author explains that if the girl's father, grandfather, brother, or paternal uncle are absent, the paternal cousin becomes her 'asaba (residuary heir) and thus her guardian (wali). In the marriage contract, the same individual can serve as guardian from the woman's side and as the groom (principal) from his own side, or as agent from both sides. The author provides two hadith proofs: (1) The Prophet's marriage to Aisha, where he was principal from his side and agent from hers; (2) The hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd where the Prophet acted as agent for both parties using a single utterance. This establishes the legal principle that one person can represent both sides in a marriage contract. The commentary notes that the paternal cousin's right to marry his cousin is valid and permissible.

Key Terms
عصبة ('asaba): A male agnatic relative who inherits as a residuary heir and has guardianship over a woman for marriage in the absence of closer relatives.
ولي (wali): A guardian with the authority to contract a woman's marriage; in this context, the paternal cousin becomes the wali in the absence of father, grandfather, etc.
أصيل (asil): The principal party in a contract, here meaning the groom acting on his own behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a paternal cousin marry his paternal cousin directly?
A) No, because the guardian must be a separate person.
B) Yes, because he is her 'asaba and can act as both guardian and groom.
C) Yes, but only if he is her appointed agent.
D) No, unless the father gives permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a paternal cousin to marry his paternal cousin by acting as both guardian and groom, based on the Prophet's practice.

Woman Appointing a Man to Marry Her: The Ruling of Direct Authorization
Ruling with proof: permissibility of a woman's direct authorization to a groom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman authorizing a man to marry her from himself and explain the evidence from the Prophet's marriage to Aisha.

Core Idea
A woman can authorize a man to marry her directly; the same man acts as both agent and groom.

In Hanafi fiqh, marriage is a contract that can be delegated. This lesson explores a specific scenario: a woman appoints a man as her agent to contract her marriage, but that man is also the groom. The key question is whether one person can simultaneously represent both parties. The source passage provides a clear ruling and evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the precise act being ruled upon? The woman authorizes a specific man to marry her. The ruling: it is permissible (jaza) when contracted in the presence of two witnesses.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha: the Prophet married her when she was six. In that marriage, the Prophet was both the groom (asil) and the agent (wakil) for Aisha, as her guardian (her father) delegated him.
Hadith from Bukhari no. 5134.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's role as both principal and agent establishes that one person can hold both capacities in a marriage contract. This is the proof that the man’s dual role is valid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require a separate guardian for the woman, arguing that the woman cannot directly appoint the groom as her agent. The Hanafi position relies on the prophetic example.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts this ruling as mufta bihi, supported by the clear textual evidence and the principle that delegation in marriage is permissible as long as the essential conditions (two witnesses) are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۴) واذا اذنت المرأة لرجل ان يزوجها من نفسه فعقد بحضرة شاهدين جاز. [عورت نے ایک آدمی کو اپنی شادی کا وکیل بنایا کہ وہ اپنی شادی اس عورت سے کرے۔ پس اس آدمی نے دو گواہوں کے سامنے نکحت کہہ کر اپنا نکاح اس عورت سے کر دیا تو نکاح ہو جائے گا۔] کیونکہ وہ اپنی جانب سے امیل ہوا اور عورت کی جانب سے وکیل ہوا۔ اور نکاح میں ایک ہی آدمی وکیل اور اصیل بن سکتا ہے (۲) اوپر حدیث گزری عن عائشة ان النبي عل الله تزوجها وهى بنت ست سنين (ج) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۵۱۳۴) جس میں حضور اپنی جانب سے اصیل اور حضرت عائشہ کی جانب سے وکیل تھے (۳) نکاح میں وکیل موکل کی جانب سے سفیر اور معجر ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ دونوں جانب سے وکیل نہیں بن سکتا۔
(84) If a woman authorizes a man to marry her from himself, and he contracts in the presence of two witnesses, it is permissible. [A woman made a man her agent for her marriage: that he should marry himself to this woman. So that man said 'I marry' in the presence of two witnesses, thereby performing his marriage to this woman, so the marriage is valid.] Because he becomes a principal from his own side and an agent from the woman's side. In marriage, one man can be both agent and principal. (2) The hadith passed above: from Aisha that the Prophet (ﷺ) married her when she was six years old (Bukhari, no. 5134), in which the Prophet was a principal from his side and an agent from Aisha's side. (3) In marriage, the agent is a representative and intermediary from the principal's side, therefore he cannot be an agent from both sides.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a woman may authorize a man to marry her directly, meaning that the same man acts as both the groom (principal) and her agent (wakil). The marriage is valid if contracted in the presence of two witnesses. The author explains that the man is acting as a principal for himself and as an agent for the woman. This is supported by the hadith of the Prophet's marriage to Aisha, where he was the principal from his side and her agent. The note clarifies that in marriage, an agent is a representative and intermediary, so typically cannot be agent from both sides, but here it is permissible because he is acting as agent from one side only (the woman's) and principal from his own. The ruling establishes the validity of a woman appointing a specific man to marry her.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by the woman to contract her marriage; in this case, the agent is also the groom.
أصيل (asil): The principal party, here the man acting on his own behalf as the groom.

Key Takeaway
A woman can authorize a man to marry her from himself; the marriage is valid with two witnesses, as established by the Prophet's marriage to Aisha.
