Guardian Guaranteeing the Mahr: Validity and Options
Ruling on guardian guaranteeing mahr, with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a guardian guaranteeing the mahr and identify the woman's options to claim from either the husband or the guardian.

Core Idea
A guardian's guarantee of the mahr is valid; the wife may claim from either the husband or the guardian.

This passage addresses a practical scenario in marriage: if the guardian (wali) guarantees the mahr, does that release the husband? And who can the wife demand payment from? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle of daman and a supporting hadith. Understanding this ruling helps ensure that the wife's right to the mahr is preserved without confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that if the guardian guarantees the mahr, his guarantee is valid (sahha damanuhu). This establishes the permissibility of the act.
The ruling is not obligatory but permissible (mubah) and legally effective.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a hadith of Jabir concerning Abu Qatadah guaranteeing the debt of a deceased man. Identify this hadith as the proof.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi; it is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
In the hadith, the Prophet delayed the funeral prayer until the debt was guaranteed, and later said the deceased's skin cooled only after payment. This shows the original debtor's obligation remains alongside the guarantor's. Analogously, the husband's mahr obligation remains despite the guardian's guarantee.
The analogy (qiyas) is applied: the mahr is a debt similar to the two dinars.
4
Identify the woman's option
The passage explicitly states: 'wal-mar'ati al-khiyar fi mutalabati zawjiha aw waliyiha' – the woman has the option to demand from her husband or her guardian.
She is not required to demand from both simultaneously; she may choose either.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۵) واذا ضمن الولى المهر للمرأة صح ضمانه وللمرأة الخيار في مطالبة زوجها او وليها. [عورت کو نکاح کرانے کا جو دلی تھا وہی شوہر کی جانب سے عورت کو مہر ادا کرنے کا ولی بن گیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اور عورت کو اختیار ہے کہ شوہر سے مہر کا مطالبہ کرے۔ اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ اپنے ولی سے مطالبہ کرے۔ کیونکہ وہ بھی ادا کرنے کا کفیل ہے۔ نکاح میں ولی سفیر اور معبر ہوتا ہے۔ اس پر مہر لینے کی ذمہ داری نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے وہ شوہر کی جانب سے مہر ادا کرنے کا کفیل بن سکتا ہے۔ اور چونکہ شوہر اصل ذمہ دار ہے اس لئے عورت اس سے بھی مطالبہ کر سکتی ہے۔ اور ولی کفیل ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی مطالبہ کر سکتی ہے (۲) حدیث میں دونوں سے مطالبہ کرنے کا اشارہ ہے۔ قال جابر توفى رجل فغسلناه وحنطناه وكفناه ثم اتينا النبي الله فقلنا له تصلى عليه فقال فخطا خطى ثم قال عليه دين؟ قال فقيل ديناران قال فانصرف قال فتحملهما ابو قتادة قال فاتيناه قال فقال ابو قتادة الديناران على فقال النبي حق الغريم وبرى منهما الميت قال نعم فصلى عليه رسول الله الله قال فقال له بعد ذلك بيوم ما فعل الديناران قال انما مات امس قال فعاد اليه كالغد قال قد قضيتهما فقال النبي الله الآن بردت عليه جلده (سن للبیہقی ، باب الضمان علی لمیت ج سادس ص ۱۲۴، نمبر ۱۱۴۰۵) اس حدیث میں اس وقت تک میت کی چمڑی ٹھنڈی نہیں ہوئی جب تک کہ دونوں دینارا بوقتادہ نے ادانہ کر دیئے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو دینار کی ذمہ داری اصل میت پر بھی رہی۔ اس لئے کفیل اور مکفول عنہ شوہر دونوں مہر کے ذمہ دار ہوں گے۔
(85) If the guardian guarantees the mahr for the woman, his guarantee is valid, and the woman has the option to demand from her husband or her guardian. [The one who was the guardian for the woman's marriage became the guardian for paying the mahr from the husband's side, so this is permissible. And the woman has the option to demand the mahr from the husband, and also has the option to demand from her guardian, because he is also a guarantor of payment. In marriage, the guardian is an intermediary and representative; he is not responsible for taking the mahr. Therefore he can become a guarantor for paying the mahr on behalf of the husband. And since the husband is the original obligor, the woman can demand from him as well. And the guardian is the guarantor, so she can demand from him as well. (2) The hadith indicates demanding from both. Jabir said: A man died, we washed him, perfumed him, and shrouded him, then we came to the Prophet and said: Pray over him. He stepped forward, then said: Does he have any debt? It was said: Two dinars. He turned back. Abu Qatadah said: They are on me. We came to the Prophet and Abu Qatadah said: The two dinars are on me. The Prophet said: The creditor's right? And the deceased is free of them? He said: Yes. Then the Messenger of Allah prayed over him. The next day he asked: What of the two dinars? He said: He died just yesterday. He repeated the next day, and he said: I have paid them. The Prophet said: Now his skin has grown cool. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on guarantee for the deceased, vol. 6 p. 124 no. 11405). This hadith shows that the deceased's skin did not grow cool until Abu Qatadah had paid the two dinars. This indicates that the obligation of the two dinars remained on the deceased originally. Therefore the guarantor and the guaranteed (the husband) are both responsible for the mahr.]
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a guardian can validly guarantee (daman) the mahr on behalf of the husband. Once he does so, the woman has the option to claim the mahr from either her husband (the original obligor) or her guardian (the guarantor). The author explains that the guardian, who arranged the marriage, is not originally liable for the mahr, but he may become a guarantor. The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatadah guaranteeing the debt of a deceased man. In that hadith, the Prophet delayed the funeral prayer until the debt was guaranteed, indicating that the debt remains on the deceased but the guarantor is also liable. Analogously, the husband remains primarily liable for the mahr, but the guardian as guarantor can be demanded payment. This establishes the woman's right of recourse against both.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): A guarantee or suretyship, where the guardian becomes liable for the mahr alongside the husband.
كفيل (kafil): A guarantor who undertakes payment of a debt; here the guardian becomes a kafil for the mahr.
مهر (mahr): The obligatory bridal gift from the husband to the wife, which can be guaranteed by the guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a guardian guarantees the mahr, what options does the woman have?
A) Only to demand from the husband.
B) Only to demand from the guardian.
C) To demand from either the husband or the guardian.
D) To demand from both simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The guardian's guarantee does not release the husband; the wife retains the right to claim from both.

Guardian's Guarantee of Mahr and Woman's Option to Demand
Ruling on guardian guaranteeing mahr with woman's option to claim from husband or guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a guardian's guarantee of mahr and explain the woman's right to demand from both the husband and the guardian, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A guardian's guarantee of mahr is valid; the woman may demand payment from the husband or the guarantor.

In a nikah, the guardian (wali) sometimes voluntarily guarantees the mahr to the bride. This passage clarifies the validity of such a guarantee and the woman's right to demand payment from either the husband (the principal debtor) or the guardian (the surety). The ruling is supported by a hadith analogy where a guarantor's payment does not absolve the original debtor until the debt is fully settled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'And if the guardian guarantees the mahr for the woman, his guarantee is valid.' Note that the hukm is sahih (valid).
The ruling applies only when the guardian voluntarily guarantees; he is not automatically liable.
2
Identify the parties and their roles
The husband is the original obligor of the mahr. The guardian becomes a guarantor (kafeel) from the husband's side. The woman is the creditor.
The guardian is not the debtor; he is a surety.
3
Identify the woman's option
The text states: 'the woman has the option to demand from her husband or her guardian.' She can choose either or both.
This is a legal option (khiyar) given to the woman.
4
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Jabir about a deceased man with a debt. Abu Qatadah guaranteed the debt, but the Prophet (ﷺ) still considered the deceased liable until the debt was paid.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and is zanni al-thubut.
5
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that even after a guarantee, the original debtor remains liable until payment. Similarly, the husband remains liable despite the guardian's guarantee, so the woman can demand from both.
The similarity (illah) is the continuity of the debt's obligation on the original debtor.

(85) And if the guardian guarantees the mahr for the woman, his guarantee is valid, and the woman has the option to demand from her husband or her guardian. Commentary: And if the guardian becomes a guarantor for the mahr for the woman, his being a guarantor is valid. And the woman has the option in demanding from her husband or from her guardian. The guardian who performed the marriage becomes, from the husband's side, the guardian for paying the mahr to the woman, so this is permissible. And the woman has the option to demand the mahr from the husband. And she also has the option to demand from her guardian, because he is also a guarantor for payment. In marriage, the guardian is an intermediary and an agent. He does not have the responsibility of taking the mahr. Therefore, he can become a guarantor from the husband's side for paying the mahr. And since the husband is the original responsible person, the woman can demand from him. And the guardian is the guarantor, so she can demand from him. (2) The hadith indicates demanding from both. Jabir said: A man died, and we washed him, embalmed him, and shrouded him. Then we came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said, 'Pray for him.' He took a step and then asked, 'Does he have debt?' It was said, 'Two dinars.' He turned back. Abu Qatadah assumed the responsibility. We came to him and Abu Qatadah said, 'The two dinars are on me.' The Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'The right of the creditor and the deceased is absolved from them?' He said, 'Yes.' So the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prayed for him. The next day he asked, 'What about the two dinars?' He said, 'He just died yesterday.' He returned to him the following day and he said, 'I have paid them.' The Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'Now his skin has become cool.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Daman 'an al-Mayyit, vol. 6, p. 124, no. 11405) This hadith indicates that the skin of the deceased did not cool until Abu Qatadah paid the two dinars. This shows that the debt remained the responsibility of the original deceased. Therefore, the guarantor and the one guaranteed for (the husband) both are responsible for the mahr.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the validity of a guardian guaranteeing the mahr and the woman's right to demand it from either the husband or the guardian. The text opens with the hukm: if the guardian guarantees the mahr, it is valid. The woman has the option to sue either the husband (the principal debtor) or the guardian (the surety). The commentary clarifies that the guardian who arranges the marriage becomes the husband's agent for paying the mahr, so he can become a guarantor. The woman is not restricted; she can demand from both. The proof is a hadith about debt: when Abu Qatadah guaranteed a deceased's debt, the Prophet (ﷺ) still considered the deceased liable until the debt was paid. Similarly, the husband remains liable even if the guardian guarantees. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): The act of guaranteeing payment of a debt (here mahr) by a third party.
كفيل (kafeel): The guarantor who assumes responsibility for the debt.
مهر (mahr): The mandatory bridal gift given by the husband to the wife in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

No Mahr in Fasid Nikah Before Consummation or Khalwah
Ruling on absence of mahr in fasid nikah before consummation or khalwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no mahr is due in a fasid marriage if the qadi separates the spouses before actual consummation or khalwah, and cite the athar proof from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
No mahr in fasid marriage unless actual intercourse occurs — khalwah does not trigger it.

This lesson examines the ruling on mahr in a fasid (defective) marriage when the qadi separates the couple before consummation or even after khalwah (seclusion). The Hanafi position distinguishes between valid and fasid marriages: in a valid marriage, khalwah can trigger mahr, but in a fasid marriage, only actual intercourse obligates mahr. The proof comes from the practice of the early Muslims (athar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State clearly the ruling: if the qadi separates the couple in a fasid nikah before consummation (dakhul) or before valid seclusion (khalwah), the woman is not entitled to any mahr.
This is stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Understand the Condition for Mahr
Recognize that mahr becomes obligatory only if actual sexual intercourse (dakhul) took place. Khalwah in a fasid marriage does not have the same effect as in a valid marriage.
The passage explicitly says khalwah is not equivalent to intercourse in fasid nikah.
3
Examine the Rationale
The commentary explains that a fasid nikah is like a coerced marriage; it does not take full effect before consummation. Therefore, mahr is not obligatory unless consummated.
This is a key point distinguishing fasid from valid nikah.
4
Analyze the Athar Proof
The passage cites two athar: one from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and one from Ata. Both condition mahr on actual intercourse. Without it, no mahr is due.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
5
Note the Scope
This ruling applies specifically to fasid marriage. The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may consider khalwah equivalent.
Stick to Hanafi position: only dakhul obligates mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۸۱۱] (۸۶) واذا فرق القاضى بين الزوجين في النكاح الفاسد قبل الدخول فلا مهر لها وكذلك بعد الخلوة ۔ اگر قاضی نے نکاح فاسد میں بیوی شوہر کے درمیان تفریق کرائی صحبت سے پہلے تو اس کے لئے مہر نہیں ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی خلوت کے بعد مہر نہیں ہے۔ نکاح فاسد میں قاضی نے میاں بیوی کے درمیان تفریق کرائی۔ پس اگر محبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے تفریق کرائی تو عورت کے لئے مہر نہیں ہے۔ نکاح فاسد مجبوری کے درجہ میں نکاح ہے۔ اس لئے باضابطہ محبت سے پہلے نکاح کا انعقاد نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے اس سے پہلے مہر بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ نکاح صحیح نہیں ہے اس لئے خلوت کرنا صحبت کے درجے میں نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی نے صحبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے تفریق کر دی تو مہر لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال كل نکاح فاسد نحو الذي تزوج في عدتها واشباهه ماذا من النكاح الفاسد اذا كان قد دخل بها؟ فلها الصداق ويفرق بينهما (الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۱۶۱ ما قالوافي المرأة تزوج في عدتها الها الصداق ام لا؟ ج رابع ، ص ۴ نمبر ۱۷۱۹۰) اور مصنف عبد الرزاق میں ہے۔وقال عطاء لها صداقها بما اصاب منها (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نکا تھافی عد تھاج سادس ص ۲۰۹ نمبر ۱۰۵۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ صحبت کرے گا تب عورت کو مہر ملے گا ورنہ نہیں۔
[1811] (86) And if the qadi separates between the spouses in a fasid nikah before consummation, then there is no mahr for her, similarly after khalwah. If the qadi separates between the spouses in a fasid nikah: if separation occurs before intercourse or before khalwah, then the woman has no mahr. A fasid nikah is like a marriage under compulsion. Therefore, before actual intercourse, the marriage is not formally concluded. So before that, mahr is not obligatory. And since the marriage is not valid, khalwah is not equivalent to intercourse. Therefore, if the qadi separates before intercourse or before khalwah, no mahr becomes obligatory. (2) This athar proves it: From Ibrahim: 'Every fasid nikah, such as one who marries a woman in her iddah or similar, if he had intercourse with her, then she gets the mahr, and they are separated.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 4, p. 4, no. 17190) And in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: 'Ata said: She has her mahr because of what he got from her.' (vol. 6, p. 209, no. 10532) This athar indicates that only if intercourse occurs does the woman get mahr; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a fasid (defective) marriage contract. The ruling states that if a qadi separates the couple before actual intercourse (dakhul) or before valid seclusion (khalwah), then the woman is not entitled to any mahr. The commentary explains that a fasid nikah is considered a coerced marriage; it does not take full effect before consummation, so mahr is not obligatory. Khalwah in a fasid marriage does not have the same effect as in a valid marriage. The proof comes from two athar: Ibrahim al-Nakha'i states that in a fasid marriage (like marrying during iddah), if intercourse occurred, the woman gets the mahr; otherwise not. Ata similarly affirms that mahr is due only because of intercourse. Therefore, the absence of intercourse or seclusion voids the mahr obligation.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): A marriage contract that is deficient in a condition or pillar, e.g., marrying during iddah, but not totally invalid.
خلوت (khalwah): Valid seclusion between husband and wife that is lawful and without impediment.
مهر (mahr): Bridal gift; obligation in valid marriage. In fasid marriage, only due after actual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid nikah, when does a wife become entitled to mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) As soon as the contract is made
B) After khalwah (seclusion) only
C) After actual sexual intercourse
D) Only if the qadi separates after khalwah

Key Takeaway
In a fasid nikah, mahr is only obligatory after actual consummation; khalwah does not substitute.
